Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Zakat Taken by Tyrants: Must It Be Paid Again?
Commentary on the ruling that zakat taken by tyrants is not taken again

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether zakat taken by tyrants must be paid again, and explain the reasoning behind the intra-Hanafi difference.

Core Idea
Zakat taken by tyrants must be repaid because they lack authority to distribute it to the poor, unless the payer intended it as charity.

When a tyrant ruler forcibly takes zakat from a Muslim's wealth, does that fulfill the obligation? The Hanafi school discusses two views: one requiring repayment and another allowing it to suffice if the payer made the intention of charity. In this lesson, we will explore the basis of this ruling, the concept of 'collection by protection,' and the practical guidance for the believer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a tyrant (baghi) taking zakat from a person's wealth. The matn states it is not taken again, but the commentary explains that repayment may be required depending on circumstances.
The matn's ruling is a default; the commentary provides exceptions and different views.
2
Understand 'collection by protection'
The Imam's protection (himayah) justifies tax collection. Tyrants lack such authority, so their collection is invalid, and the obligation remains.
This principle underlies the entire discussion.
3
Compare zakat and kharaj
Zakat must be repaid because its recipients are the poor; tyrants do not give it to them. Kharaj (land tax) does not need to be repaid because its recipients are fighters, and tyrants are fighters themselves.
This distinction is key to understanding the fatwa from Al-Hidayah.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference
Some scholars hold that if the payer intended the payment as charity (sadaqah) for the tyrant, it suffices, because tyrants are considered poor due to their obligations. The more cautious view (ihiyat) requires repayment.
The story of Muhammad and Ali ibn Isa illustrates that even a wealthy governor may be considered poor due to debts.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
For hidden wealth (amwal batina), al-Walwalji's view that it is not permissible to pay to tyrants is the fatwa. For apparent wealth, the best practice is to give directly to the poor. However, if paid to tyrants with charity intention, some scholars consider it sufficient.
The authority weight is from later fatwa collections (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

His statement: (And if the tyrants take the tithe, land tax, and zakat, it is not taken again) meaning it is not taken a second time because the Imam did not protect them, and collection is by protection. He said in al-Hidayah: they gave a fatwa that they should repeat it (pay again) except for the land tax, because they (the tyrants) are recipients of the land tax as they are fighters, and zakat's recipients are the poor and they do not give it to them. And it is said: if he intended when paying to give charity to them, it is dropped from him, and similarly payment to every oppressor because they, due to the obligations upon them, are poor, and the first is more cautious. He generalised in zakat so it includes apparent and hidden wealth. Therefore he said in al-Mabsut: the correct view is that the owners of wealth, if they intend when paying to the oppressors to give charity to them, all of that is dropped from them, and likewise all that is taken from a man of levies and confiscations because what is in their hands is the wealth of Muslims and what is upon them of obligations exceeds their wealth, so they are in the position of debtors and the poor. So much so that Muhammad said: it is permissible to give charity to Ali ibn Isa ibn Mahan, the governor of Khurasan, and he was an amir in Balkh, an expiation for an oath became obligatory on him, so he asked and they gave him a fatwa to fast, so he started crying and said to his retinue: they say to me that the obligations upon you exceed the wealth you have, so your expiation is the expiation of an oath of one who owns nothing. He said in Fath al-Qadir: based on this, if he bequeaths one third of his wealth to the poor and then pays to the unjust sultan, it is dropped. Qadikhan mentioned it in al-Jami' al-Saghir. Based on this, their rejection of Yahya ibn Yahya, the student of Malik, when he gave a fatwa to some kings of the Maghreb... His statement: (They gave him a fatwa to fast etc.) this contradicts what was presented from al-Kashf al-Kabir that expiation with wealth does not prevent the obligation of debt according to the correct view, so this is based on the opposite of the correct view. His statement: (not harmful) is the predicate of the subject which is... valid for an expiation upon him with fasting not necessary, and their reasoning that it is consideration for the suitable known nullification is not necessary because it may be for the consideration we mentioned of their poverty, not because it is more difficult on him than manumission to be the suitable known nullification. And that they have wealth and what they took and mixed with it, and that is destruction if it cannot be distinguished from it according to Abu Hanifa: they own it and must guarantee it, so much so that they said zakat is obligatory on them for it and it is inherited from them, not harmful because their liability is occupied with its equivalent, and the debtor to the extent of what is in his hand is poor. (End) And the apparent view of al-Sarakhsi is that there is no difference between apparent and hidden wealth. Al-Walwalji affirmed the non-permissibility for hidden wealth, he said: and by it fatwa is given because the sultan has no authority over zakat on hidden wealth, so why take it? (End) In al-Zahiriyyah: the best for the owner of apparent wealth is to give the zakat to the poor himself because these people do not place zakat in its proper places. As for the land tax, they do place it in its proper places because the land tax is for fighters and there are no fighters. (End) In al-Tabyin: the condition of their taking the land tax and the like is established, so that even if they do not take from him for years, and it is with them, nothing is taken from them also, due to what we mentioned. (End) And 'the other' in his statement 'and it is with them' refers to the one upon whom the land tax and the like is due, and the plural pronoun in 'with them' refers to the tyrants, i.e., the one upon whom is due according to the tyrants. And he generalized regarding the one upon whom the land tax is due, so it includes the dhimmi like the Muslim. And the author indicated that if a harbi becomes Muslim in dar al-harb and stays there for years then comes out to us, the Imam does not take zakat from him due to lack of protection, and we give him a fatwa to pay it if he knows of its obligation, otherwise there is no zakat on him because the address did not reach him, which is a condition of obligation.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn ruling that when tyrant rulers (bughat) take the tithe, land tax, and zakat, it is not taken again from the taxpayer. The author explains the rationale: the Imam did not provide protection, so the collection is invalid. Then he discusses differing fatwas. According to Al-Hidayah, one must repays zakat because the tyrants do not distribute it to the poor, but for land tax it suffices because it is for fighters. Another view says that if the payer intended charity for the rulers, it drops the obligation. The author notes that the rulers are considered debtors and poor due to the obligations on them, so paying them as charity is valid. There is a difference of opinion regarding apparent versus hidden wealth: some say it applies to both, while al-Walwalji affirms non-permissibility for hidden wealth. The passage also discusses the case of a harbi who converts to Islam and resides in dar al-harb: he does not have to pay zakat for past years because the obligation did not reach him. The commentary is based on reasoning (istihsan) and citations from earlier Hanafi authorities.

Key Terms
بغاة (bughat): Tyrants or unjust rulers who take taxes and zakat by force.
ثني (thani): Taking zakat twice from the same property in the same year; prohibited by hadith.
حماية (himayah): Protection provided by the ruler; collection of taxes is justified by the protection given.
غارمون (gharimun): Debtors; one of the eight categories of zakat recipients.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the ruling for kharaj (land tax) different from zakat when taken by tyrants?
A) Because kharaj is not a religious obligation.
B) Because tyrants are considered fighters, which is the recipient of kharaj.
C) Because kharaj is paid by non-Muslims.
D) Because tyrants have no authority over kharaj.

Key Takeaway
When zakat is taken by a tyrant, repayment is required unless the payer intended it as charity for the tyrant, but the cautious view (ahwat) is to repay, and for hidden wealth it is not permissible to pay the tyrant at all.

Accelerating Zakat for Multiple Years or Multiple Nisabs
Commentary on validity of accelerating zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid acceleration of zakat and apply them to determine whether a given scenario is permissible.

Core Idea
Accelerating zakat is valid if you already own a nisab and your wealth remains above nisab all year.

This lesson explains the ruling on paying zakat in advance for multiple years or on multiple nisabs. The key is that you must already be a zakatable person at the time of payment, and your wealth must not fall below nisab during the year. The hadith 'No thani in sadaqah' supports this, as acceleration does not constitute taking zakat twice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is accelerating zakat (ta'jil) for multiple years or multiple nisabs. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) under certain conditions.
The passage begins by clarifying that thani (double charging) is prohibited, but acceleration does not cause thani.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'لا ثني في الصدقة' (No thani in sadaqah). This is a Sunnah ahad with zanni thubut but qati dalala.
The hadith prohibits taking zakat twice from the same property in one year.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith's prohibition of thani implies that prepaying zakat on a different property or for a future year is allowed, as it does not involve double charging.
The passage also discusses scenarios where assets are converted, showing that the new asset is treated separately.
4
Note the conditions for validity
Three conditions are mentioned: (1) The payer must already own a complete nisab at the time of acceleration. (2) The nisab must not break during the year. (3) The nisab must be complete at the end of the year.
If any condition is violated, the acceleration becomes invalid and the zakat must be paid again.
5
Consider the implications and edge cases
The passage also discusses how to handle assets that are converted (e.g., selling zakatable livestock) and the addition of new wealth. These details reinforce that the validity of acceleration hinges on maintaining the nisab.
The author also addresses a potential contradiction about the poverty of rulers, but the core ruling remains clear.

ثم باعها يضم ثمنها إلى ما عنده لخروجها عن الزكاة فصار كمال آخر فلم يؤد إلى الثني، وكذا لو جعل العبد المؤدى زكاته للخدمة ثم باعه يضم ثمنه إلى ما عنده، ولو أدى صدقة الفطر عن عبد الخدمة أو أدى عشر طعامه ثم باعه ثمنه إلى ما عنده لأنه ليس ببدل مال أديت الفطرة عنه لأن الفطرة إنما تجب بسبب رأس يمونه ويلي عليه دون المالية ألا ترى أنها تجب عن أولاده الأحرار والثمن بدل المالية، والعشر إنما يجب بسبب أرض نامية لا بالخارج فلم يثبت الاتحاد حتى لو باع الأرض النامية لا يضم ثمنها إلى ما عنده عند أبي حنيفة. ومن عنده نصابان من جنس واحد أحدهما ثمن إبل مزكاة فاستفاد نصاباً من جنسها فإنه يضم إلى أقربهما حولاً لأنهما استويا في علة الضم، وترجح | أحدهما باعتبار القرب لكونه أنفع للفقراء، ولو كان المستفاد ربحاً أو ولداً ضمه إلى أصله، وإن كان أبعد حولاً لأنه يرجح باعتبار التفرع والتولد لأنه تبع وحكم التبع لا يقطع الأصل، ولو أدى زكاة الدراهم ثم اشترى بها سائمة وعنده من جنسها سائمة لم يضمها إليه لأنها بدل مال أديت الزكاة عنه ا هـ . موضع اتفاقاً قوله (ولو عجل ذو نصاب لسنين أو لنصب (صح) أما الأول فلأنه أدى بعد سبب الوجوب فيجوز لسنة ولسنين كما إذا كفر بعد الجرح وأما الثاني فلأن النصاب الأول هو الأصل في السببية والزائد عليه تابع له. قيد بقوله ذو نصاب لأنه لو عجل قبل أن يملك تمامه ثم تم الحول على النصاب لا يجوز وفيه شرطان آخران : أن لا ينقطع النصاب في أثناء الحول، وأن يكون كاملاً في آخره. فتفرع على الأول أنه لو عجل ومعه نصاب ثم هلك كله بما مر : ومراده قوله «وكونهم» وفي النهر : ولا يخفى أن فيه تدافعاً ظاهراً وذلك أن وجوب الزكاة عليه يؤذن بغنائه وجواز الصرف إليه يقتضي فقره وتنبه لما قيدنا به المسألة فيما مر فإنه مما لا غنى عنه هنا ا هـ . قوله وينبغي أن يقيد بما إذا لم يكن له مال غيره يوفي منه الكل أو البعض فإن كان زكي ما قدر على وفائه إلى آخر ما قدمناه وبه يندفع التدافع عن كلام المحقق لأن كونهم فقراء إذا لم يكن لهم مال غير ما استهلكوه ووجوب الزكاة عليهم إذا كان لهم مال غيره أما إذا لم يكن فلا وجوب، ولا يخفى أنه خلاف المتبادر من كلامهم هنا على أنه قليل الجدوى لأن الزكاة حينئذ تكون لما له الغير المأخوذ من الناس لا المستهلك أن كلامهم فيه فبقي إشكال المؤلف السابق على حاله، وما نقلناه عن التتارخانية هناك مؤيد له حيث صرح فيها بأنه لا زكاة في تلك الأموال وإن بلغت نصاباً لأنه مديون ولعل في المسألة خلافاً كما قال في الشرنبلالية. وفي الفتح ما يفيد الخلاف لنقله بصيغة
Realisation of 'thani' in charity, because thani is imposing zakat twice on one owner for one property in one year, and it is negated by his statement (peace be upon him): 'No thani in sadaqah.' And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he combines, combining wealth. If he makes grazing animals fodder after having paid zakat on them, then sells them, he adds their price to what he has because they have exited zakat, so they become another wealth, so thani does not occur. Similarly, if he made the slave on whom he paid zakat into a servant, then sells him, he adds his price to what he has. And if he paid sadaqat al-fitr for a servant slave, or paid the tithe of his food, then sold him, his price is added to what he has because it is not a substitute for wealth for which fitr was paid, because fitr is only obligatory due to a head that he supports and cares for, not due to wealth. Do you not see that it is obligatory for his free children? And the price is a substitute for wealth. And the tithe is only obligatory due to productive land, not due to the output; thus union is not established, so that if he sells the productive land, he does not add its price to what he has according to Abu Hanifa. And whoever has two nisabs of the same type, one being the price of camels on which zakat was paid, and then acquires a nisab of the same type, he adds it to the closer of the two in terms of year because they are equal in the cause of addition, and one is preferred by closeness because it is more beneficial for the poor. And if the acquired is profit or offspring, he adds it to its origin, even if it is further in year because it is preferred by branch and generation because it is a follower, and the ruling of the follower does not cut off the origin. And if he paid zakat on dirhams, then bought with them grazing animals, and he has grazing animals of the same type, he does not add them to them because they are a substitute for wealth for which zakat was paid. (End) Regarding the consensus statement: His saying (And if one who owns a nisab accelerates for years or for multiple nisabs, it is valid). As for the first, because he paid after the cause of obligation, so it is permissible for one year and for years, just as if he expiates after a wound. As for the second, because the first nisab is the origin in causation, and the additional is subordinate to it. He restricted by saying 'one who owns a nisab' because if he accelerates before he owns the complete nisab, then the year completes on the nisab, it is not valid. And there are two other conditions: that the nisab does not break during the year, and that it is complete at its end. A branch on the first: if he accelerates while he has a nisab, then it all perishes... and his meaning... His statement: 'and that they' and in al-Nahr: it is not hidden that there is an apparent contradiction in it: that the obligation of zakat on him indicates his wealth, and the permissibility of giving to him indicates his poverty. Noted what we qualified the issue with earlier, for it is indispensable here. (End) His statement: it should be qualified by the case where he has no other wealth from which he can pay the whole or part; if he did, it would be zakat on what he can pay... and by this the contradiction in the words of the investigator is repelled, because they are poor if they have no wealth other than what they consumed, and zakat is obligatory on them if they have other wealth. As for if they do not, then there is no obligation. And it is not hidden that this contradicts the apparent meaning of their words here, and it is of little benefit because then the zakat is on the acquired wealth of others, not the consumed, and their words are about it, so the author's previous difficulty remains. And what we transmitted from al-Tatarkhaniyyah there supports it, where it states that there is no zakat on those funds even if they reach a nisab because he is in debt. Perhaps there is a difference of opinion on the issue, as said in al-Shurnublaliyyah. And in al-Fath, what indicates the difference, because he narrated it with the formula...
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that accelerating zakat for multiple years or multiple nisabs is valid. It first clarifies the concept of 'thani' (taking zakat twice) and shows that accelerating does not lead to thani because the accelerated payment is on a different asset or a different year. The author discusses various cases where assets are converted or combined, and whether their values are added to existing nisab. These include grazing animals turned into fodder, slaves, sadaqat al-fitr, tithe on land, and profits from an existing nisab. The general rule is that if the asset exits the category of zakatable wealth, its price is added to other assets; if it is a substitute for wealth on which zakat was already paid, it is not added. Then the commentary explains the conditions for valid acceleration: the payer must already own a complete nisab at the time of acceleration, the nisab must not be broken during the year, and it must be complete at the end. The passage also addresses a potential contradiction regarding the poverty of the rulers and the obligation of zakat on them, concluding that there is a nuance depending on whether they have other wealth.

Key Terms
ثني (thani): Taking zakat twice from the same property in the same year; prohibited.
تعجيل (ta'jil): Paying zakat in advance before the end of the year or for multiple years.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that makes zakat obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is accelerating zakat for multiple years NOT valid?
A) If the nisab breaks during the year.
B) If the person accelerates before owning a complete nisab.
C) If the nisab is not complete at the end of the year.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Accelerating zakat is valid if you meet the conditions of nisab continuity and have a nisab at the time of payment.

Advance Payment of Zakat (Ta'jil): Conditions and Rulings
Ruling on advance zakat with conditions and collector scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid advance payment of zakat and determine whether a given scenario results in valid zakat, voluntary charity, or liability.

Core Idea
Advance zakat is valid only if the nisab remains complete throughout the year.

Paying zakat before its due date (ta'jil) is a practical need for many Muslims, but Hanafi fiqh sets precise conditions to ensure it counts as the obligatory zakat. This lesson unpacks the ruling from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, explaining when advance payment is valid, when it becomes voluntary charity (nafl), and the intricate responsibilities of the payer and the official collector (sa'i). Understanding these nuances prevents common mistakes that could leave one's zakat obligation unfulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
The act is paying zakat before the completion of the lunar year (ta'jil). The general ruling is that it is valid (sahih) under specific conditions. First, identify the hukm level based on the Hanafi position.
The ruling's validity hinges on conditions that must persist through the year.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author provides a qiyas (analogy): advance payment is likened to performing kaffarah (expiation) after a wound. In both cases, the cause of obligation exists partially, permitting advance fulfillment. Identify this qiyas and its logical structure.
The cause (sabab) of zakat is ownership of nisab; once it is present, payment is allowed even before the year completes.
3
Trace the Conditions
Two key conditions are stated: (1) the nisab must not be interrupted during the year, and (2) it must be complete at the end of the year. List these and understand why each is necessary: interruption breaks the causal link, and deficiency at year-end means the obligation never fully matured.
These conditions are derived from the general principle that zakat is due only after a full year of nisab ownership.
4
Analyze the Collector Scenarios
The passage details 21 subcases based on three categories: payment in the collector's hands, consumed by collector, or given to poor. Trace the ruling for each: if the nisab fails, the payment becomes nafl (voluntary charity) and the owner may retrieve it from the collector.
The distinction between livestock (saimah) and money matters: livestock nisab is not completed by debt, so advance payment on livestock is more restrictive.
5
Apply the Rules to Multiple Nisabs
The second part covers advance payment for multiple nisabs (e.g., owning 200 dirhams but paying zakat for 1000). It is valid only if the payer acquires the additional wealth within the same year. Understand this as a condition of eventual ownership.
This prevents paying zakat on wealth one does not yet possess.

قوله (ولو عجل ذو نصاب لسنين أو لنصب (صح) أما الأول فلأنه أدى بعد سبب الوجوب فيجوز لسنة ولسنين كما إذا كفر بعد الجرح وأما الثاني فلأن النصاب الأول هو الأصل في السببية والزائد عليه تابع له. قيد بقوله ذو نصاب لأنه لو عجل قبل أن يملك تمامه ثم تم الحول على النصاب لا يجوز وفيه شرطان آخران : أن لا ينقطع النصاب في أثناء الحول، وأن يكون كاملاً في آخره. فتفرع على الأول أنه لو عجل ومعه نصاب ثم هلك كله بما مر : ومراده قوله «وكونهم» وفي النهر : ولا يخفى أن فيه تدافعاً ظاهراً وذلك أن وجوب الزكاة عليه يؤذن بغنائه وجواز الصرف إليه يقتضي فقره وتنبه لما قيدنا به المسألة فيما مر فإنه مما لا غنى عنه هنا ا هـ . قوله وينبغي أن يقيد بما إذا لم يكن له مال غيره يوفي منه الكل أو البعض فإن كان زكي ما قدر على وفائه إلى آخر ما قدمناه وبه يندفع التدافع عن كلام المحقق لأن كونهم فقراء إذا لم يكن لهم مال غير ما استهلكوه ووجوب الزكاة عليهم إذا كان لهم مال غيره أما إذا لم يكن فلا وجوب، ولا يخفى أنه خلاف المتبادر من كلامهم هنا على أنه قليل الجدوى لأن الزكاة حينئذ تكون لما له الغير المأخوذ من الناس لا المستهلك أن كلامهم فيه فبقي إشكال المؤلف السابق على حاله، وما نقلناه عن التتارخانية هناك مؤيد له حيث صرح فيها بأنه لا زكاة في تلك الأموال وإن بلغت نصاباً لأنه مديون ولعل في المسألة خلافاً كما قال في الشرنبلالية. وفي الفتح ما يفيد الخلاف لنقله بصيغة

عمالته
ثم استفاد فتم الحول على النصاب لم يجز المعجل بخلاف ما إذا بقي في يده منه شيء، وعلى الثاني ما لو عجل شاة . عن أربعين وحال الحول وعنده تسعة وثلاثون فإن كان صرفها إلى الفقراء فالمعجل نفل بخلاف ما إذا أدى بعد الحول إلى الفقير وانتقص النصاب بأدائه فإن/ الزكاة واجبة، وإن كانت قائمة في يد الساعي فالصحيح وقوعها زكاة فلا يستردها لأن الدفع إلى المصدق لا يزيل ملكه عن المدفوع، ولا فرق بين السوائم والنقود في هذا، ولا فرق بين أن تكون الزكاة في يد الساعي حقيقة أو استهلكها أو أنفقها على نفسه قرضاً أو أخذها الساعي من عمالته لأنه كقيام العين حكماً بخلاف ما إذا صرفها الساعي إلى الفقراء أو إلى نفسه وهو فقير فإنه كصرفها بنفسه فلا يجوز المعجل كما لو ضاعت من يد الساعي قبل الحول ووجدها بعده فلا زكاة وللمالك أن يستردها فلو لم يستردها حتى دفعها الساعي إلى الفقراء لم يضمن إلا إن كان المالك نهاه ثم اعلم أن وقوعها زكاة فيما إذا أخذها الساعي من إنما هو في غير السوائم، أما في السوائم فلا تقع زكاة لنقصان النصاب ويستردها المالك ويضمن الساعي قيمتها لو باعها ويكون الثمن له وإنما كان كذلك في السائمة لأنه لما خرجت عن مالك المعجل بذلك السبب فحين تم الحول يصير ضامناً بالقيمة والسائمة لا يكمل نصابها بالدين بخلاف نصاب الدراهم لأنه يكمل بالدين وهذا كله إذا لم يستفد قدر ما عجل ولم ينتقص ما عنده، فإن استفاده صار المؤدى زكاة في الوجوه كلها من وقت التعجيل وإلا يلزم هنا كون الدين زكاة عن العين في بعض الوجوه ولا يجب عليه زكاة المستفاد، وإن انتقص ما في يده فلا تجب في الوجوه كلها فيسترد إن كان في يد الساعي وإن استهلكها أو أكلها قرضاً أو بجهة العمالة ضمن. ولو تصدق بها على الفقراء أو نفسه وهو فقير لا يضمن إلا إن تصدق بها بعد الحول فيضمن عنده علم بالنقصان أو لم يعلم . وعندهما: إن علم وإن كان نهاه ضمن عند الكل، وأما الفقير فلا رجوع عليه في شيء من الصور لأنه وقع صدقة تطوعاً لو لم يجز المعجل عنها .
والحاصل أن وجوه
هذه المسألة ثلاثة وكل وجه على سبعة لأن المعجل إما أن يكون في يد الساعي أو استهلكه أو أنفقه على نفسه قرضاً أو عمالة أو صدقة أو صرفه إلى الفقراء أو ضاع من يد الساعي قبل الحول فهي إحدى وعشرون، وقد علم أحكامها وبسطه في شرح الزيادات لقاضيخان والمسألة الثانية - أعني ما إذا عجل لنصب بعد ملك نصاب واحد . مقيدة بما إذا ملك ما عجل عنه في سنة التعجيل ، فلو كان عنده مائتا درهم فعجل زكاة ألف، فإن استفاد مالاً أو ربح حتى صارت ألفاً ثم تم الحول وعنده ألف فإنه يجوز التعجيل
«قالوا تجب فيه الزكاة فإنها تذكر فيما فيه خلاف ا.هـ. فليتأمل. وقدمنا تمام الكلام على ذلك . أوائل كتاب الزكاة .
His statement: (And if a possessor of nisab pays in advance for years or for nisabs, it is valid). As for the first, because he paid after the cause of obligation, so it is permissible for one year and for years, just as if he performed expiation after a wound. And as for the second, because the first nisab is the origin in causality, and the excess is subsidiary to it. He restricted it by 'possessor of nisab' because if he pays in advance before he owns its completion, then the year is completed on the nisab, it is not valid. And in it are two other conditions: that the nisab does not break during the year, and that it is complete at its end. So it branches from the first: if he paid in advance while having a nisab, then all of it perished... as previously mentioned. And his intent is his statement 'and they are'. And in al-Nahr: it is not hidden that there is apparent contradiction: that zakat being obligatory indicates his richness, and permissibility of giving to him necessitates his poverty. Be mindful of what we have restricted the issue in what preceded, for it is essential here. It ends. His statement: It should be restricted to when he has no other property from which to pay all or part; if he has, he will pay what he can... up to what we have presented. And by it the contradiction is removed from the scholar's statement, because they are poor when they have no property other than what they have consumed, and zakat is obligatory on them when they have other property. But if not, then no obligation. And it is not hidden that this contradicts the understood from their words here, and it is of little benefit because the zakat then would be for the property taken from people, not the consumed property, so the author's previous problem remains. And what we have quoted from al-Tatar Khaniyya supports it, where it states that there is no zakat on those properties even if they reach a nisab because the person is a debtor. Perhaps there is a difference of opinion on the matter as stated in al-Shurnbulaliyya. And in al-Fath what indicates a difference, as he transmitted it in the form of... Page 389 [change]. Book of Zakat, Chapter on Sheep. His agency. Then he gained, and the year was completed on the nisab, the advanced payment is not valid, contrary to if something remained in his hand. And on the second: if he paid in advance a sheep out of forty, and the year passed while he had thirty-nine, then if he gave it to the poor, the advanced payment is supererogatory, contrary to if he paid after the year to the poor and the nisab decreased by his payment, for then zakat is obligatory. And if (the zakat) is still in the hands of the collector, the correct view is that it falls as zakat, so he does not take it back, because payment to the official does not remove his ownership of what was paid. There is no difference between grazing livestock and money in this. There is no difference between the zakat being in the hands of the collector actually, or he consumed it, or spent it on himself as a loan, or the collector took it from his agency, because it is like the presence of the asset in legal effect, contrary to if the collector gave it to the poor or to himself while being poor, for that is like giving it himself, so the advance is not valid, just as if it was lost from the collector's hand before the year and he found it after, then no zakat is due and the owner may retrieve it. If he does not retrieve it until the collector gives it to the poor, he is not liable unless the owner had forbidden him. Then know that its falling as zakat when the collector takes it is only for non-livestock; as for livestock, it does not fall as zakat because of the nisab deficiency, and the owner retrieves it and the collector guarantees its value if he sells it, and the price is for him. This is because with livestock, since it left the owner by that cause, when the year completes, he becomes liable for its value, and the livestock nisab is not completed by debt, unlike the nisab of dirhams because it is completed by debt. All this is if he did not gain the amount he advanced and did not decrease what he had. If he gained it, then the payment becomes zakat in all forms from the time of advancement; otherwise it would entail debt being zakat for the asset in some forms, and he does not owe zakat on the acquired wealth. If what he had decreased, then it is not obligatory in all forms; so he retrieves it if it is with the collector, and if he consumed it or ate it as a loan or through agency, then he is liable. And if he gave it in charity to the poor or to himself while poor, he is not liable unless he gave it after the year, then he is liable in his view whether he knew of the deficiency or not. And according to both (students): if he knew, and if he had forbidden him, he is liable according to all. As for the poor person, he has no recourse in any of the forms because it occurred as voluntary charity if the advance did not cover it. The summary: the aspects of this issue are three, and each aspect has seven possibilities: because the advanced payment is either in the hands of the collector, or he consumed it, or spent it on himself as a loan or as agency fee, or charity, or gave it to the poor, or it was lost from the collector's hand before the year; so they are twenty-one rulings. Their legal rulings are known and elaborated in Sharh al-Ziyadat by Qadikhan. And the second issue – that is, if he advances for nisabs after owning one nisab – is restricted to when he owns what he advances for in the year of advancement. So if he has two hundred dirhams and pays in advance zakat for a thousand, then he gains property or profit until it becomes a thousand, and the year completes while he has a thousand, then the advance is valid. They said: Zakat is obligatory on it because it is mentioned in matters where there is a difference. It ends. So ponder. And we have already presented the complete discussion on that at the beginning of the book of Zakat.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the ruling of paying zakat in advance (ta'jil al-zakat) for multiple future years or for additional nisabs beyond what one currently owns. The author begins by examining the statement from Kanz al-Daqa'iq: 'If a possessor of nisab pays in advance for years or for nisabs, it is valid.' The commentator explains two scenarios: (1) advance for future years is valid because the cause of obligation (ownership of nisab) is present, analogous to performing expiation after a wound (the cause of obligation exists even before the full time). (2) Advance for additional nisabs (e.g., owning one nisab but paying zakat for two) is valid because the first nisab is the root of causality, and the excess is subsidiary. Two conditions are stated: the nisab must not break during the year and must be complete at the end. The text then discusses the apparent contradiction: how can a person be both rich (zakat payer) and poor (eligible for zakat)? The resolution is that if the poor person has only consumed property, he is poor and eligible; but if he has other property, zakat is due on him. The following part details numerous scenarios involving the official collector (sa'i) receiving the advance payment. The key ruling: if the nisab decreases before the end of the year, the advance payment is invalid and the owner can retrieve it; but if it remains intact, the payment is valid as zakat. The collector's handling affects liability: if the collector gives the payment to the poor before the year ends, it is considered voluntary charity (nafl), not zakat. The text also distinguishes between livestock (sa'imah) and money: for livestock, the nisab is not completed by debt, unlike dirhams, so advance payment on livestock is more restricted. The summary lists twenty-one subcases based on three main categories (payment with collector, consumed, etc.) and seven possibilities for each. Finally, the second main issue: advancing zakat for multiple nisabs based on future acquisition; it is valid only if the person actually acquires the additional wealth within the same year.

Key Terms
تعجيل الزكاة (taʿjīl al-zakāt): Paying zakat before it becomes due, i.e., before the completion of the lunar year.
ساعي (sāʿī): The official collector of zakat appointed by the ruler or imam.
سائمة (sāʾimah): Grazing livestock (camels, cattle, sheep/goats) that are raised for milk, breeding, or meat, and are not working animals.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory; in this context, if the advance payment does not cover the zakat obligation, it becomes voluntary charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person pays zakat in advance for two years. At the end of the first year, his nisab has decreased below the threshold. What is the ruling on his advance payment for the first year?
A) The payment is valid as zakat because he paid in advance.
B) The payment becomes voluntary charity (nafl) and he must pay zakat again.
C) The payment is invalid and must be returned.
D) The payment counts for the second year only.

Key Takeaway
Advance zakat payment is valid in the Hanafi school, but only if the nisab remains complete throughout the year; a decrease in nisab turns the payment into voluntary charity and requires the owner to pay zakat again.

Zakat — Almsgiving
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Validity of Advance Zakat (Ta'jeel) When Paid to the Collector
Opening section of the ruling on ta'jeel conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which advance zakat paid to the collector is valid, and identify when it becomes voluntary charity.

Core Idea
Advance zakat is only valid if the nisab remains intact at year-end; any decrease or acquisition changes the ruling.

When zakat is paid before the year ends (ta'jeel), the validity depends on the condition of the nisab when the year completes. This lesson examines the core rules: if the owner acquires more wealth or loses part of the nisab, the advance payment may become invalid or require adjustment. We also explore the role of the collector (sa'i) in preserving the payment's status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic condition for ta'jeel
Read the opening: 'If he acquired [wealth] and the year completed on the nisab, the advance is not valid.' This establishes that ta'jeel requires the nisab to remain completely under the owner's possession at year-end.
The nisab must be physically present, not just a debt.
2
Analyze the scenario of partial nisab
The next example: 'if he advanced a sheep for forty and had thirty-nine at year-end, if he gave to the poor, it's naf (voluntary).' This shows that if the nisab is deficient, the advance becomes charity.
Contrast with payment after the year when nisab decreases—that remains wajib.
3
Understand the effect of payment to the collector
The text then states: 'if it remained in the collector's hand, the correct view is it counts as zakat.' Paying the sa'i is like keeping the property in trust; ownership doesn't transfer until the year ends.
This applies to cash and livestock alike.
4
Distinguish when the collector consumes or disposes of the payment
If the collector consumes it, spends it on himself as a loan, or uses it for his wages, it is 'like it stands' and still counts as zakat. But if he gives it to the poor or to himself while poor, it is like the owner gave it directly—invalid as ta'jeel.
The key is whether the payment leaves the collector's possession in a way that mimics owner disposal.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on liability
Towards the end of this section: if the collector gives to the poor after the year, Abu Hanifa holds the owner liable, while the Sahibayn say only if he forbade. This shows a difference in reasoning about the collector's agency.
All agree if the owner forbade, the collector is liable.

Source Text

ثم استفاد فتم الحول على النصاب لم يجز المعجل بخلاف ما إذا بقي في يده منه شيء، وعلى الثاني ما لو عجل شاة . عن أربعين وحال الحول وعنده تسعة وثلاثون فإن كان صرفها إلى الفقراء فالمعجل نفل بخلاف ما إذا أدى بعد الحول إلى الفقير وانتقص النصاب بأدائه فإن/ الزكاة واجبة، وإن كانت قائمة في يد الساعي فالصحيح وقوعها زكاة فلا يستردها لأن الدفع إلى المصدق لا يزيل ملكه عن المدفوع، ولا فرق بين السوائم والنقود في هذا، ولا فرق بين أن تكون الزكاة في يد الساعي حقيقة أو استهلكها أو أنفقها على نفسه قرضاً أو أخذها الساعي من عمالته لأنه كقيام العين حكماً بخلاف ما إذا صرفها الساعي إلى الفقراء أو إلى نفسه وهو فقير فإنه كصرفها بنفسه فلا يجوز المعجل كما لو ضاعت من يد الساعي قبل الحول ووجدها بعده فلا زكاة وللمالك أن يستردها فلو لم يستردها حتى دفعها الساعي إلى الفقراء لم يضمن إلا إن كان المالك نهاه ثم اعلم أن وقوعها زكاة فيما إذا أخذها الساعي من إنما هو في غير السوائم، أما في السوائم فلا تقع زكاة لنقصان النصاب ويستردها المالك ويضمن الساعي قيمتها لو باعها ويكون الثمن له وإنما كان كذلك في السائمة لأنه لما خرجت عن مالك المعجل بذلك السبب فحين تم الحول يصير ضامناً بالقيمة والسائمة لا يكمل نصابها بالدين بخلاف نصاب الدراهم لأنه يكمل بالدين وهذا كله إذا لم يستفد قدر ما عجل ولم ينتقص ما عنده، فإن استفاده صار المؤدى زكاة في الوجوه كلها من وقت التعجيل وإلا يلزم هنا كون الدين زكاة عن العين في بعض الوجوه ولا يجب عليه زكاة المستفاد، وإن انتقص ما في يده فلا تجب في الوجوه كلها فيسترد إن كان في يد الساعي وإن استهلكها أو أكلها قرضاً أو بجهة العمالة ضمن. ولو تصدق بها على الفقراء أو نفسه وهو فقير لا يضمن إلا إن تصدق بها بعد الحول فيضمن عنده علم بالنقصان أو لم يعلم . وعندهما: إن علم وإن كان نهاه ضمن عند الكل، وأما الفقير فلا رجوع عليه في شيء من الصور لأنه وقع صدقة تطوعاً لو لم يجز المعجل عنها . والحاصل أن وجوه هذه المسألة ثلاثة وكل وجه على سبعة لأن المعجل إما أن يكون في يد الساعي أو استهلكه أو أنفقه على نفسه قرضاً أو عمالة أو صدقة أو صرفه إلى الفقراء أو ضاع من يد الساعي قبل الحول فهي إحدى وعشرون، وقد علم أحكامها وبسطه في شرح الزيادات لقاضيخان
Then he acquired [additional wealth] and the year completed on the nisab, the advance payment is not valid, unlike if something remained in his hand. And on the second [scenario]: if he advanced a sheep for forty and the year completed while he had thirty-nine, then if he gave it to the poor, the advance is a voluntary charity, unlike if he paid after the year to the poor and the nisab decreased by his payment, then zakat is obligatory. And if it remained in the collector's hand, the correct [view] is that it counts as zakat, so he cannot reclaim it because giving to the collector does not remove ownership from what was given. There is no difference between grazing livestock and cash in this, and no difference between the zakat actually being in the collector's hand or he consumed it, or spent it on himself as a loan, or the collector took it from his wages, because it is like the property standing effectively, unlike if the collector gave it to the poor or to himself while he is poor, then it is like he gave it himself, so the advance is not valid, just as if it was lost from the collector's hand before the year and he found it after, then no zakat is due, and the owner can reclaim it. If he does not reclaim it until the collector gives it to the poor, he is not liable unless the owner forbade him. Then know that its falling as zakat when the collector took it is only for non-livestock. As for livestock, it does not fall as zakat due to deficiency of nisab, and the owner reclaims it, and the collector is liable for its value if he sold it, and the price is for him. And that is the case for livestock because when it left the owner's possession by that cause, at the completion of the year he becomes liable for its value, and the nisab of livestock is not completed by debt, unlike the nisab of dirhams because it is completed by debt. All this if he did not acquire the amount he advanced and his [remaining] property did not decrease. If he acquired it, then what was paid becomes zakat in all respects from the time of advancement, otherwise it would entail debt being zakat for property in some respects, and he is not obligated to pay zakat on the acquired property. If his [remaining] property decreased, then it is not obligatory in all respects, so he reclaims it if it is with the collector, and if the collector consumed it, or ate it as a loan, or via the wage channel, he is liable. And if he gave it in charity to the poor or to himself while he is poor, he is not liable unless he gave it in charity after the year, then he is liable according to him [Abu Hanifa] whether he knew the deficiency or not. According to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]: if he knew, and if he forbade him, all agree he is liable. As for the poor person, there is no recourse against him in any scenario because it fell as voluntary charity if the advance was not valid. The summary: the aspects of this issue are three, and each aspect has seven [subcategories], because the advanced payment is either in the collector's hand, or he consumed it, or spent it on himself as a loan or wage, or as charity, or he gave it to the poor, or it was lost from the collector's hand before the year. So they are twenty-one, and their rulings have been learned, and it is elaborated in Sharh al-Ziyadat by Qadikhan.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on advance payment of zakat (ta'jeel) in complex scenarios. The author explains that if the owner pays zakat before the year ends and then acquires additional wealth such that the nisab is maintained, the advance payment is invalid because the nisab condition changed. However, if some of the advanced property remains with the collector (sa'i) at year-end, the payment is valid. The text then enumerates 21 scenarios based on three main categories: what happens to the payment after the collector receives it. The Hanafi position is that the payment counts as zakat if the collector retains it, but if the collector gives it away or the property is lost, different rules apply. The commentary follows the author's order, first explaining the base ruling, then the exceptions for livestock versus cash, then the 21-fold categorization. All examples are Hanafi and based on the six books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah). The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as the text references al-Mabsut and other core works.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jeel): Advance payment of zakat before the end of the lunar year (hawl).
الساعي (as-sa'i): The official zakat collector appointed by the ruler or community.
السوائم (as-sawa'im): Grazing livestock (cattle, sheep, camels) kept for production, on which zakat is due.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person pays zakat in advance to the collector, and the collector gives it to the poor before the year ends, what is the status of the payment?
A) The payment is still valid as zakat because it was paid to the collector.
B) The payment is invalid and becomes voluntary charity (nafl).
C) The payment is a loan to the collector.
D) The owner can reclaim the payment.

Key Takeaway
The validity of advance zakat hinges on the nisab being complete at year-end and the payment not being disposed of by the collector in a way attributable to the owner.

Condition for Valid Advance Zakat on a Nisab
Ruling statement: conditions for advance zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for advance zakat (ta'jeel) to be valid and apply it to scenarios involving acquisition, destruction, and mistaken payment.

Core Idea
Advance zakat requires ownership of the property within the same lunar year; otherwise it does not count.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a key condition for advance zakat: you must own what you paid zakat on during that same year. The text uses examples of camels, dirhams, and dinars to illustrate when the advance counts and when it does not. We will work through these conditions step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is paying zakat in advance (ta'jeel) for a nisab larger than the one you currently own. The ruling: valid only if you eventually own the property for which you advanced within the same year.
2
List the core condition
The passage states: 'It is conditioned upon him owning that for which he advanced in the year of advancement.' This is the primary condition.
Year of advancement is the lunar year in which the payment is made.
3
Apply to the basic example
A person has 200 dirhams and pays zakat for 1000. If he later acquires 800 more (total 1000) within the same year, the advance is valid. If he does not acquire, the advance does not count.
This shows that future acquisition can fulfill the condition.
4
Work through the camel and dirham examples
For camels: advancing for pregnant camels and their young – if the young are born within the year, it counts. For dirhams: white and black dirhams – if one type is destroyed, the advance may count for the other if the genus is the same.
When the genus is the same, specification is irrelevant.
5
Note exceptions and clarifications
Mistaken payment (e.g., paying extra because you thought you owned more) can be counted as an advance for the next year. Once zakat is validly paid to a poor person, subsequent changes (rich, death, apostasy) do not affect validity.
These exceptions are derived from Fatawa of Qadikhan and al-Walwaljiya.

Source Text

وعنده ألف فإنه يجوز التعجيل «قالوا تجب فيه الزكاة فإنها تذكر فيما فيه خلاف ا.هـ. فليتأمل. وقدمنا تمام الكلام على ذلك . أوائل كتاب الزكاة . في  عن كتاب الزكاة فصل في الغنم وسقط عنه زكاة الألف، وإن تم لم يوجد المعجل عنه في سنة التعجيل ففقد الشرط فلم يجز عما تحمله في الثانية، وهو المراد من نفي الجواز. وليس المراد نفي الجواز مطلقاً لظهور أنه يقع عما في ملكه وقت التعجيل في الحول الثاني فهو تعجيل زكاة ما في ملكه لسنتين لأن التعيين في الجنس الواحد لغو، وكذا لو كان له ألف درهم بيض وألف سود فعجل خمسة وعشرين عن البيض فهلكت البيض قبل تمام الحول ثم تم لا زكاة عليه في السود ويكون المخرج عنها ، وكذا عكسه. وكذا لو عجل عن الدنانير وله دراهم ثم هلكت الدنانير كان ما عجل عن الدراهم باعتبار القيمة وكذا عكسه. قيدنا بالهلاك لأنه لو عجل أحد المالين ثم استحق المال الذي عجل عنه قبل الحول لم يكن المعجل عن الباقي، وكذا لو استحق بعد الحول لأن في الاستحقاق عجل عما لم يملكه فبطل تعجيله. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان. وبما ذكرناه اندفع ما في فتح القدير من الاعتراض على الفرع الأول المنقول من الفتاوى كما لا يخفى. وقيدنا بكون الجنس متحداً لأنه لو كان له خمس من الإبل وأربعون من الغنم فعجل شاة عن أحد الصنفين ثم هلك لا يكون عن الآخر، ولو كان له عين ودين فعجل عن العين فهلكت قبل الحول جاز عن الدين، وإن هلكت بعده لا يقع عنه، وفي الولوالجية وغيرها : رجل عنده أربعمائة درهم فظن أن عنده خمسمائة درهم فأدى زكاة خمسمائة فله أن يحتسب الزيادة للسنة الثانية لأنه أمكن أن تجعل الزيادة تعجيلاً .اهـ. فقولنا فيما مضى يشترط أن يملك ما عجل عنه في حوله يستثنى منه ما إذا عجل غلطاً عن شيء يظن أنه في ملكه . ثم اعلم أنه لو عجل زكاة ما له فأيسر الفقير قبل تمام الحول أو مات أو ارتد جاز عن الزكاة لأنه كان مصرفاً وقت الصرف فصح الأداء إليه فلا ينتقض بهذه العوارض. كذا في الولوالجية.
The second issue – i.e., when he advances [zakat] for a nisab after owning one nisab. It is conditioned upon him owning that for which he advanced in the year of advancement. So if he had two hundred dirhams and advanced the zakat of a thousand, then he acquired property or profit until it became a thousand, then the year completed and he had a thousand, the advancement is valid. [It is said: Zakat is obligatory on it, but it is mentioned where there is a difference. End. So consider. And we have already completed the discussion on that at the beginning of the Book of Zakat.] On page 392: And the zakat of the thousand falls from him. If the year completed and he did not acquire anything, then later acquired, the advanced does not count for its zakat. When the year completes from the time of acquisition, he must pay zakat. This is stated in al-Mabsut and clarified by al-Asbijabi, al-Kaki, al-Sighnaqi and others. This is what appears in the Fatawa of Qadikhan: if he had five pregnant camels (meaning gravid) and he advanced two sheep for them and for what is in their wombs, then they became five before the year, his advance suffices. If he advanced for what they carry in the second year, it is not permissible. End. Because when he advanced for what they carry in the second year, that for which he advanced was not present in the year of advancement, so the condition lost, so it did not count for what they carry in the second year. That is the meaning of negation of permissibility. It does not mean absolute negation, because clearly it falls for what he owned at the time of advancement in the second year, so it is an advancement of zakat for what he owns for two years, because specification within a single genus is of no effect. Similarly, if he had a thousand white dirhams and a thousand black dirhams, and he advanced twenty-five for the white, then the white were destroyed before the completion of the year, then the year ends, no zakat is due on the black, and what was paid counts for them. And similarly the opposite. And similarly if he advanced for dinars while having dirhams, then the dinars were destroyed, what he advanced counts for the dirhams by value, and similarly the opposite. We restricted to destruction because if he advanced one of the two properties, then that for which he advanced was lost before the year, the advance does not count for the remaining. Similarly if it was lost after the year, because in the loss he advanced for what he did not own, so his advance is void. As in the Fatawa of Qadikhan. And with what we have mentioned, the objection in Fath al-Qadir on the first branch from the Fatawa is refuted, as is clear. And we restricted to the genus being the same because if he had five camels and forty sheep, and he advanced a sheep for one of the two types, then it perishes, it does not count for the other. If he has ayn (cash) and dayn (debt), and he advanced for the ayn, then the ayn perishes before the year, it counts for the dayn. If it perishes after, it does not count. In al-Walwaljiya and others: A man had four hundred dirhams and thought he had five hundred, so he paid zakat of five hundred. He may count the extra for the second year, because it is possible to make the extra an advancement. End. So our earlier statement that it is conditional upon owning that for which he advanced within his year is excepted for the case where he advanced mistakenly for something he thought he owned. Then know: if he advanced the zakat of his property and the poor person becomes rich before the year's end, or dies, or apostatizes, it is valid for the zakat, because he was a valid recipient at the time of payment, so payment to him is sound, and these subsequent events do not invalidate it. As in al-Walwaljiya.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage delves into the second major issue of advance zakat: when a person who owns one full nisab wishes to pay zakat in advance on a larger nisab (e.g., he has 200 dirhams but pays zakat for 1000). The key condition is that he must own the property for which he advanced the zakat at some point during the same lunar year in which he made the advance. If he later acquires enough to make the full nisab, the advance is valid; if he does not, the advance does not count for that amount. The text then illustrates with examples from camels (pregnant and their young), dirhams (white and black), and dinars vs. dirhams. It also discusses the effect of destruction or loss of the property: if the property for which zakat was advanced is lost before the year ends, the advance may still count for another similar property if the genus is the same. An exception is made for mistaken payment (e.g., someone pays extra zakat thinking he owns more than he does), where the extra can be counted as an advance for the next year. Finally, the passage notes that once payment is validly made to a poor person, subsequent changes in that person's status do not affect the validity of the zakat. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah, as references to al-Mabsut and Fatawa of Qadikhan indicate reliance on core Hanafi texts.

Key Terms
المسألة الثانية (al-mas'alah al-thaniyah): The second issue regarding advance zakat: paying for a nisab after owning one nisab.
سنة التعجيل (sanat al-ta'jeel): The lunar year in which the advance payment is made.
تعجيل (ta'jeel): The act of paying zakat before the end of the lunar year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person has 200 dirhams and pays zakat in advance for 1000 dirhams, then acquires 800 dirhams later in the same year, what is the ruling?
A) The advance is invalid because he did not own 1000 at the time of payment.
B) The advance is valid because he owned the property for which he advanced within the same year.
C) The advance is valid only if he also pays zakat on the newly acquired 800 immediately.
D) He must pay zakat again because the advance was not based on actual ownership.

Key Takeaway
Advance zakat is valid only if the property for which it is paid is owned during the same lunar year; otherwise, the payment does not fulfill the zakat obligation for that amount.

Advance Payment of 'Ushr: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ta'jeel
Ruling on ta'jeel for 'ushr before crop is ripe, with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi imams' positions on advancing 'ushr before crop emergence and identify the reasoning (talil) behind each view.

Core Idea
The cause of 'ushr (sabab) triggers the advance payment dispute—does it exist at planting or only at crop emergence?

In this passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author discusses the permissibility of paying 'ushr in advance. While all agree that payment is allowed after the crop appears (but before ripening), there is a disagreement on whether one may pay even earlier, after planting but before the crop emerges. This lesson examines the reasoning behind the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling context
Determine what 'ushr is and what 'advance payment' (ta'jeel) means in this context. Note that 'ushr is a 10% zakat on agricultural produce from non-kharaj land.
The passage distinguishes between payment after the crop appears (agreed) and payment after planting but before emergence (disputed).
2
Extract the positions of each imam
From the passage, note: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit advancing 'ushr after planting; Muhammad does not. Also note that all imams forbid advancing 'ushr before planting or grafting.
Abu Yusuf additionally differs on the time of obligation (ripening vs. emergence), but still permits advance payment.
3
Analyze the talil (reasoning)
Muhammad argues that the payment is for the actual crop (al-hadith), not the seed (al-badhr); since no crop exists, the advancement lacks its object. The others argue that the cause (sabab) of 'ushr—the land and seed—already exists at planting, so advancement is valid.
The sabab is key: is it the land+seed or the actual produce?
4
Understand the sabab concept
The passage hints that the cause of 'ushr is 'the land producing growth' (al-ard al-namiyah bi al-kharij). This is central to the dispute: when is this cause fully realized?
The hashiya from al-Nahr comments on the cause, but the passage cuts off before complete clarification.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Muhammad requires the farmer to wait until the crop emerges; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow payment right after planting, giving earlier discharge of zakat obligation.
This difference affects the timing of financial planning for the farmer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف بجواز التعجيل بعد ملك النصاب إلى جواز تعجيل عشر زرعه بعد النبات قبل الإدراك أو عشر الثمر بعد الخروج قبل البلوغ لأنه تعجيل بعد وجود السبب، وبعدم جوازه قبل ملك النصاب إلى عدم جواز تعجيل العشر قبل الزرع أو قبل الغرس. واختلف في تعجيله قبل النبات بعد الزرع أو بعدما غرس الشجر قبل خروج الثمرة؛ فعند محمد لا يجوز لأن التعجيل للحادث لا للبذر ولم يحدث شيء، من قوله : (يستثنى منه ما إذا عجل غلطاً الخ قال في النهر الظاهر أنه لا استثناء وأن هذا المسألة الأولى قوله : ( بعد النبات الخ) سيأتي في باب العشر أن سببه الأرض النامية بالخارج حقيقة وأن وقته وقت خروج الزرع وظهور الثمرة عند أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف وقت الإدراك، وعند
And the author indicated by 'permissibility of advancement after owning the nisab' the permissibility of advancing the 'ushr of his crop after the plant [appears] before ripening, or the 'ushr of fruit after it appears before ripening, because it is advancement after the cause exists. And by 'its impermissibility before owning the nisab' [he indicated] the impermissibility of advancing the 'ushr before planting or before grafting. And there is disagreement on its advancement before the plant [emerges] after planting or after grafting the tree before the fruit appears. According to Muhammad, it is not permitted because the advancement is for the event (the crop), not for the seed, and nothing has happened. From his statement: '(Excepted is when he advances mistakenly...)' He said in al-Nahr: It is apparent that there is no exception, and that this is the first issue. His statement: '(After the plant...) will come in the chapter on 'ushr that its cause is the land producing growth in reality, and its time is the time of emergence of the crop and appearance of fruit according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Abu Yusuf it is the time of ripening, and according [to Muhammad? cut off]
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage discusses the advance payment of 'ushr (tithe on agricultural produce) within the framework of advance zakat. The author (Ibn Nujaym) interprets the perfector's (al-Kanz) statement that advance payment is allowed after owning the nisab to apply also to 'ushr: one may pay 'ushr in advance after the crop appears but before it is ripe, because the cause of 'ushr (land and seed) has already occurred. However, advance payment is not allowed before planting or grafting, as no cause exists. Then an intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned regarding advancing 'ushr after planting but before the crop emerges. Imam Muhammad holds it is not valid because the advancement relates to the eventual crop, not the seed, and no crop yet exists. The hashiya (from al-Nahr) then comments on a previous exception about mistaken advance, suggesting it is not an exception but a different issue. The passage ends mid-sentence, stating that Abu Hanifa considers the time of 'ushr as when the crop appears, Abu Yusuf as when it ripens, and Muhammad's view is cut off. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as this is from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq.

Key Terms
العشر (al-'ushr): The tithe (10%) due on agricultural produce from land that is not subject to kharaj.
السبب (as-sabab): The cause that makes 'ushr due: land ownership and cultivation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, is it valid to pay 'ushr in advance after planting but before the crop emerges?
A) Yes, because the cause of 'ushr exists from the time of planting.
B) No, because the advancement is for the crop event, not the seed, and no crop yet exists.
C) Yes, but only if the land is irrigated by rainfall.
D) No, because 'ushr cannot be paid in advance at all.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on advancing 'ushr before crop emergence hinges on whether the sabab (cause) is complete at planting or only at emergence.

General Rulings of Advance Zakat (Ta'jil): Conditions and Exceptions
Rulings on conditions of ta'jil, existence of property, destruction vs reclamation, mistaken payments, and recipient status changes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the property advanced for must exist at the time of ta'jil, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving destruction, reclamation, mistaken payments, and changes in recipient status.

Core Idea
Ta'jil is valid only if the property advanced for exists at payment; destruction preserves validity, reclamation voids it, and recipient changes do not affect it.

Advancing zakat before the year ends is permissible in the Hanafi school, but it comes with strict conditions. This lesson explores the key requirement that the property must exist at the time of advancement, and examines how destruction (halk), reclamation (istihqaq), mistaken payments, and changes in the recipient's status affect the validity of the advance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that ta'jil is permissible after owning nisab but is subject to conditions.
2
State the existence condition
The property for which zakat is advanced must be in existence and owned at the time of advancement.
This is the core condition derived from Fatawa Qadikhan.
3
Distinguish destruction from reclamation
If the property is destroyed (halk) after advancement, the advance counts for similar property. If the property is reclaimed (istihqaq), the advance is void because the property was not owned.
Destruction: advance valid. Reclamation: advance void.
4
Apply the mistaken payment exception
If someone mistakenly pays more zakat than owed, the excess can be considered an advance for the next year.
Exception to the rule that property must exist for that specific payment.
5
Note the effect of recipient changes
If the poor recipient becomes wealthy, dies, or apostatizes after receiving the advance, the zakat is still valid because the recipient was eligible at the time of payment.
Stability of payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسقط عنه زكاة الألف، وإن تم الحول ولم يستفد شيئاً ثم استفاد فالمعجل لا يجزئ عن زكاتها، فإذا تم الحول من حين الاستفادة كان عليه أن يزكي صرح به في المبسوط وأفاده الأسبيجابي والكاكي والسغناقي وغيرهم. وبهذا ظهر ما في فتاوى قاضيخان من أنه لو كان له خمس من الإبل الحوامل يعني الحبالى فعجل شاتين عنها وعما في بطنها ثم نتجت خمساً قبل الحول أجزأه ما عجل، وإن عجل عما تحمل في السنة الثانية لا يجوز اهـ . لأنه لما عجل عما تحمله في الثانية لم يوجد المعجل عنه في سنة التعجيل ففقد الشرط فلم يجز عما تحمله في الثانية، وهو المراد من نفي الجواز. وليس المراد نفي الجواز مطلقاً لظهور أنه يقع عما في ملكه وقت التعجيل في الحول الثاني فهو تعجيل زكاة ما في ملكه لسنتين لأن التعيين في الجنس الواحد لغو، وكذا لو كان له ألف درهم بيض وألف سود فعجل خمسة وعشرين عن البيض فهلكت البيض قبل تمام الحول ثم تم لا زكاة عليه في السود ويكون المخرج عنها ، وكذا عكسه. وكذا لو عجل عن الدنانير وله دراهم ثم هلكت الدنانير كان ما عجل عن الدراهم باعتبار القيمة وكذا عكسه. قيدنا بالهلاك لأنه لو عجل أحد المالين ثم استحق المال الذي عجل عنه قبل الحول لم يكن المعجل عن الباقي، وكذا لو استحق بعد الحول لأن في الاستحقاق عجل عما لم يملكه فبطل تعجيله. كذا في فتاوى قاضيخان. وبما ذكرناه اندفع ما في فتح القدير من الاعتراض على الفرع الأول المنقول من الفتاوى كما لا يخفى. وقيدنا بكون الجنس متحداً لأنه لو كان له خمس من الإبل وأربعون من الغنم فعجل شاة عن أحد الصنفين ثم هلك لا يكون عن الآخر، ولو كان له عين ودين فعجل عن العين فهلكت قبل الحول جاز عن الدين، وإن هلكت بعده لا يقع عنه، وفي الولوالجية وغيرها : رجل عنده أربعمائة درهم فظن أن عنده خمسمائة درهم فأدى زكاة خمسمائة فله أن يحتسب الزيادة للسنة الثانية لأنه أمكن أن تجعل الزيادة تعجيلاً .اهـ. فقولنا فيما مضى يشترط أن يملك ما عجل عنه في حوله يستثنى منه ما إذا عجل غلطاً عن شيء يظن أنه في ملكه . ثم اعلم أنه لو عجل زكاة ما له فأيسر الفقير قبل تمام الحول أو مات أو ارتد جاز عن الزكاة لأنه كان مصرفاً وقت الصرف فصح الأداء إليه فلا ينتقض بهذه العوارض. كذا في الولوالجية. وأشار المصنف بجواز التعجيل بعد ملك النصاب إلى جواز تعجيل عشر زرعه بعد النبات قبل الإدراك أو عشر الثمر بعد الخروج قبل البلوغ لأنه تعجيل بعد وجود السبب، وبعدم جوازه قبل ملك النصاب إلى عدم جواز تعجيل العشر قبل الزرع أو قبل الغرس. واختلف في تعجيله قبل النبات بعد الزرع أو بعدما غرس الشجر قبل خروج الثمرة؛ فعند محمد لا يجوز لأن التعجيل للحادث لا للبذر ولم يحدث شيء، من قوله : (يستثنى منه ما إذا عجل غلطاً الخ قال في النهر الظاهر أنه لا استثناء وأن هذا المسألة الأولى قوله : ( بعد النبات الخ) سيأتي في باب العشر أن سببه الأرض النامية بالخارج حقيقة وأن وقته وقت خروج الزرع وظهور الثمرة عند أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف وقت الإدراك، وعند محمد عند التنقية والجذاذ ا.هـ. وبه علم أنه على قول أبي حنيفة ليس ما ذكره هنا بتعجيل بل هو أداء في وقته .
And the zakat of one thousand is dropped from him. If the year completed and he did not acquire anything, then he acquired, the advanced payment does not suffice for its zakat. When the year completes from the time of acquisition, he must pay zakat—explicitly stated in al-Mabsut and related by al-Asbajabi, al-Kaki, al-Sighnaqi, and others. By this, what is in Fatawa Qadikhan becomes clear: if one has five pregnant camels and advances two sheep for them and what is in their bellies, then the camels calve within the year, his advance suffices. But if he advances for what she carries in the second year, it is not permissible—because he advanced for what is carried in the second year, the thing advanced for does not exist in the year of advancement, so the condition is lost, so it does not suffice for what she carries in the second year, and that is the intended meaning of negation of permissibility. It is not intended to negate permissibility absolutely because it appears that it falls on what he owns at the time of advancement in the second year, so it is an advancement of zakat of what he owns for two years because specification in the same category is futile. Similarly, if he has one thousand white dirhams and one thousand black dirhams, and he advances twenty-five for the white, then the white are destroyed before the completion of the year, then the year completes—no zakat is due on the black, and the amount paid is for them. Similarly its opposite. Similarly, if he advances for dinars while he has dirhams, then the dinars are destroyed, what he advanced is for the dirhams by consideration of value, and similarly its opposite. We restricted to destruction because if he advanced one of the two properties, then the property for which he advanced is reclaimed (due to a claim) before the year, the advanced payment is not for the remaining—similarly if reclaimed after the year, because in reclamation he advanced for what he did not own, so his advancement is void. Thus in Fatawa Qadikhan. By what we mentioned, the objection in Fath al-Qadir on the first branch transmitted from the Fatawa is repelled, as is not hidden. And we restricted to the category being unified because if he has five camels and forty sheep, and he advances a sheep for one of the two types, then it is destroyed, it is not for the other. If he has cash and debt, and he advances for the cash, then the cash is destroyed before the year, it is permissible for the debt; if destroyed after the year, it does not fall on it. In al-Walwaljiyah and others: a man has four hundred dirhams, and he thinks he has five hundred dirhams, so he pays zakat of five hundred—he may count the excess for the second year because it is possible to make the excess an advancement. So our statement earlier 'it is required that he owns what he advances for in its year' has an exception: when he advances mistakenly for something he thinks he owns. Then know that if he advances zakat of his wealth, and the poor person becomes wealthy before the completion of the year, or dies, or apostatizes—it is valid for the zakat because he was a valid recipient at the time of payment, so the payment to him is valid and it is not invalidated by these accidents. Thus in al-Walwaljiyah. The author (of Kanz al-Daqaiq) indicated by the permissibility of advancement after owning the nisab to the permissibility of advancing 'ushr of his crop after it appears before ripening, or 'ushr of fruit after it emerges before it ripens—because it is advancement after the existence of the cause. And by its impermissibility before owning the nisab to the impermissibility of advancing 'ushr before sowing or before planting. And there is disagreement on advancing it before the plant appears after sowing or after planting the trees before the fruit appears: according to Muhammad it is not permissible because advancement is for what comes into being, not for the seed, and nothing has come into being. From his statement: '(the exception is made from it when he advances mistakenly...)' al-Nahr said: apparently there is no exception, and this is the first issue. His statement: '(after the plant...)' will come in the chapter of 'ushr that its cause is the land that grows by what emerges, truly, and its time is the time of emergence of the crop and appearance of the fruit according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Abu Yusuf the time of ripening, and according to Muhammad the time of threshing and harvesting. By this it is known that according to Abu Hanifa, what is mentioned here is not advancement but payment at its due time.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the rulings of ta'jil (advance payment of zakat). The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the conditions and various scenarios. He begins by stating that if one advances zakat before the completion of the year and later acquires additional wealth during the year, the advance does not cover the new wealth. The year for the new wealth starts from its acquisition, so zakat on the new wealth must be paid separately. He then clarifies a ruling from Fatawa Qadikhan: if someone has five pregnant camels and advances two sheep for them and their expected offspring, and the camels give birth within the year, the advance is valid. But if he advances for the offspring of the second year (i.e., future offspring not yet conceived), it is invalid because the property did not exist at the time of advancement. However, the advance is not absolutely invalid—it actually counts as a payment for the existing camels in the second year, making it an advance for two years. The author then discusses analogous cases with different types of currency (white and black dirhams, gold and silver). He emphasizes that the key condition is that the property for which zakat is advanced must exist at the time of advancement. If it is destroyed before the year ends, the advance is valid and covers similar property; if it is reclaimed (e.g., due to a legal claim), the advance is void because the property was not owned. He notes an exception: if someone mistakenly pays zakat thinking he has more wealth than he actually does, the excess can be counted as an advance for the next year. Additionally, if the recipient becomes wealthy, dies, or apostatizes after receiving the advance, the zakat is still valid because the recipient was eligible at the time of payment. The author then connects this to 'ushr (crop tax). The matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) allows advancing 'ushr after the crop appears but before it is ripe. This leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, advancing 'ushr before the crop appears (e.g., after sowing) is not permissible because the cause (the land's productivity) has not yet generated the crop. Abu Yusuf permits it because the land becomes productive after sowing. Abu Hanifa holds that the time for 'ushr is when the crop appears, so paying after appearance is actually payment at the proper time, not advancement. The preferred view is to avoid ta'jil due to the disagreement.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jil): Advanced payment of zakat before its due date (end of the lunar year).
حول (hawl): The lunar year that must pass while the property is in one's possession for zakat to become due.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth subject to zakat (e.g., 200 dirhams or 20 dinars).
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers zakat obligation; for 'ushr it is land that produces crops.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has 400 dirhams but mistakenly thinks he has 500 and pays zakat on 500. According to the passage, what happens to the extra payment?
A) It is invalid and must be recovered.
B) It can be counted as an advance for the next year.
C) It is considered charity, not zakat.
D) It is valid only if the recipient returns it.

Key Takeaway
The validity of ta'jil depends on the existence of the property at the time of payment; destruction preserves it, reclamation voids it, and mistaken payments are an exception.

Zakat — Almsgiving

7 min
The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Advancing 'Ushr Before the Crop Appears
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on advancing 'ushr before crop appears.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on advancing 'ushr before the crop appears, and explain the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
The three Hanafi imams differ on whether paying 'ushr after sowing but before the crop appears is valid ta'jil or not.

While the general rule allows ta'jil after the cause (sabab) exists, the application to 'ushr reveals a subtle disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Each imam has a different understanding of when the obligation for 'ushr is triggered and whether early payment is an advance or payment at the proper time. This lesson dissects their positions and the thamarah al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute is about advancing 'ushr after sowing but before the crop appears or before it is ripe. Is it valid ta'jil?
2
Muhammad's position
Muhammad says it is not permissible because the crop does not yet exist. Ta'jil is for what comes into being, not for seed.
3
Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf permits it because the land becomes productive after sowing, so the cause exists.
4
Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the time for 'ushr is when the crop appears; thus payment after appearance, even before ripening, is not ta'jil but payment at its proper time.
5
Determine the practical difference
According to Muhammad, the payment does not count and must be repeated; according to Abu Yusuf, it suffices; according to Abu Hanifa, it is not ta'jil but proper timing.
The thamarah al-khilaf: whether the payer must pay again at harvest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسقط عنه زكاة الألف، وإن تم الحول ولم يستفد شيئاً ثم استفاد فالمعجل لا يجزئ عن زكاتها، فإذا تم الحول من حين الاستفادة كان عليه أن يزكي صرح به في المبسوط وأفاده الأسبيجابي والكاكي والسغناقي وغيرهم. وبهذا ظهر ما في فتاوى قاضيخان من أنه لو كان له خمس من الإبل الحوامل يعني الحبالى فعجل شاتين عنها وعما في بطنها ثم نتجت خمساً قبل الحول أجزأه ما عجل، وإن عجل عما تحمل في السنة الثانية لا يجوز اهـ . لأنه لما عجل عما تحمله في الثانية لم يوجد المعجل عنه في سنة التعجيل ففقد الشرط فلم يجز عما تحمله في الثانية، وهو المراد من نفي الجواز. وليس المراد نفي الجواز مطلقاً لظهور أنه يقع عما في ملكه وقت
