Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe on the rulings of ta'jil (advance payment of zakat). The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the conditions and various scenarios. He begins by stating that if one advances zakat before the completion of the year and later acquires additional wealth during the year, the advance does not cover the new wealth. The year for the new wealth starts from its acquisition, so zakat on the new wealth must be paid separately. He then clarifies a ruling from Fatawa Qadikhan: if someone has five pregnant camels and advances two sheep for them and their expected offspring, and the camels give birth within the year, the advance is valid. But if he advances for the offspring of the second year (i.e., future offspring not yet conceived), it is invalid because the property did not exist at the time of advancement. However, the advance is not absolutely invalid—it actually counts as a payment for the existing camels in the second year, making it an advance for two years. The author then discusses analogous cases with different types of currency (white and black dirhams, gold and silver). He emphasizes that the key condition is that the property for which zakat is advanced must exist at the time of advancement. If it is destroyed before the year ends, the advance is valid and covers similar property; if it is reclaimed (e.g., due to a legal claim), the advance is void because the property was not owned. He notes an exception: if someone mistakenly pays zakat thinking he has more wealth than he actually does, the excess can be counted as an advance for the next year. Additionally, if the recipient becomes wealthy, dies, or apostatizes after receiving the advance, the zakat is still valid because the recipient was eligible at the time of payment. The author then connects this to 'ushr (crop tax). The matn (Kanz al-Daqaiq) allows advancing 'ushr after the crop appears but before it is ripe. This leads to an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, advancing 'ushr before the crop appears (e.g., after sowing) is not permissible because the cause (the land's productivity) has not yet generated the crop. Abu Yusuf permits it because the land becomes productive after sowing. Abu Hanifa holds that the time for 'ushr is when the crop appears, so paying after appearance is actually payment at the proper time, not advancement. The preferred view is to avoid ta'jil due to the disagreement.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jil): Advanced payment of zakat before its due date (end of the lunar year).
عشر ('ushr): Zakat on agricultural produce, typically 10% of the crop.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers zakat obligation; for 'ushr it is land that produces crops.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the thamarah al-khilaf in the dispute on advancing 'ushr before the crop appears?
A) The amount of 'ushr payable changes.
B) The time of payment affects the obligation to pay again.
C) The validity of the harvest as a whole.
D) The eligibility of the recipient.

Key Takeaway
The three Hanafi imams differ on advancing 'ushr before the crop appears; the mufta bihi is to avoid advancing due to the ikhtilaf.

Zakat on Gold and Silver: Nisab and Rate
Opens zakat al-mal chapter: nisab and rate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab and zakat rate for gold and silver, explain the hadith proof, and distinguish between the 'wajib' and 'fard' terminology in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Core Idea
Zakat on 200 dirhams of silver or 20 mithqals of gold is due at a rate of 2.5% (rub' al-'ushr).

This passage opens the Zakat al-Mal chapter, clarifying that 'mal' here primarily means cash (gold/silver) and trade goods. The author, following al-Quduri, uses 'wajib' for zakat and cites the hadith establishing the nisab and rate. We will dissect the ruling, its proof, and the subtle intra-Hanafi debate about whether the obligation is at the level of fard or wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zakat on gold and silver. The ruling is wajib (obligatory). Note that the author uses 'wajib' but the stronger view is fard (see later).
The term 'wajib' here reflects a debate on epistemological certainty.
2
State the nisab values
Silver: 200 dirhams (5 uqiya, each uqiya = 40 dirhams). Gold: 20 mithqals.
These thresholds are mass-transmitted (mutawatir) according to some scholars.
3
Calculate the zakat due
The rate is rub' al-'ushr (1/4 of 1/10 = 1/40 = 2.5%). For silver: 5 dirhams on 200. For gold: half a mithqal on 20.
Memorize: 200 dirhams → 5 dirhams; 20 mithqals → 0.5 mithqal.
4
Locate the dalil
The hadith in Muslim: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awaq of silver.' The companion hadith for gold is also cited. These are ahad but the measures are defended as mutawatir.
The hadith provides both the nisab and the rate (by implication of previous practice).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب زكاة المال نقد ما تقدم أيضاً زكاة مال لأن المال كما روي عن محمد كل ما يتملكه الناس من وعروض وحيوان وغير ذلك إلا أن في عرفنا يتبادره من اسم المال النقد والعروض. وقدم الفضة على الذهب في بعض المصنفات اقتداء بكتب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قوله (يجب في مائتي درهم وعشرين مثقالاً ربع العشر) وهو خمسة دراهم في المأتين ونصف مثقال في العشرين . والعشر بالضم أحد الأجزاء العشرة وإنما وجب ربع العشر لحديث مسلم «ليس فيما دون خمس أوراق من الورق صدقة والأوقية أربعون رهما كما رواه الدار قطني. ولحديث علي وغيره في الذهب. وعبر المصنف بالوجوب تبعاً للقدوري في قوله الزكاة واجبة قالوا: لأن بعض مقاديرها وكيفياتها ثبتت بأخبار الآحاد وقد صرح السيد نكر كان في شرح المنار أن مقادير الزكوات ثبتت بالتواتر كنقل القرآن وإعداد الركعات وهذا يقتضى كفر جاحد المقدار في الزكوات. قيد بالنصاب لأن ما دونه لا زكاة فيه ولو كان نقصاناً يسيراً يدخل بين الوزنين
Chapter of zakat of wealth. It has also preceded that zakat is on wealth, because wealth, as is narrated from Muhammad, is everything that people own of cash, goods, animals, and other than that, except that in our convention the name 'wealth' immediately brings to mind cash and goods. And silver is placed before gold in some works following the books of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. His statement: 'It is wajib on two hundred dirhams and twenty mithqals a quarter of a tenth' (rub' al-'ushr). That is five dirhams in two hundred, and half a mithqal in twenty. Al-'ushr (with damm on 'ayn) is one of ten parts. And only a quarter of a tenth is wajib because of the hadith of Muslim: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awaq of silver' and the uqiya is forty dirhams as related by al-Daraqutni, and the hadith of 'Ali and others concerning gold. The author expressed it as 'wajib' following al-Quduri in his statement 'zakat is wajib'. They said: because some of its measures and modalities are established by ahad reports, and al-Sayyid Nukran stated in Sharh al-Minar that the measures of zakat are established by tawatur like the transmission of the Qur'an and the numbers of rak'at, and this entails the disbelief of one who denies the measure in zakat. It is restricted by nisab because what is below it has no zakat, even if the deficiency is slight that falls between the two weights.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on zakat of mal (wealth) from Kanz al-Daqaiq, with commentary from Ibn Nujaym. The author first clarifies that the term 'mal' here refers specifically to cash (gold and silver) and trade goods, although in broader Hanafi definition, mal includes everything of value. Zakat is wajib (obligatory) on 200 dirhams of silver or 20 mithqals of gold, at the rate of 1/40 (rub' al-'ushr). For silver, this equals 5 dirhams per 200; for gold, half a mithqal per 20. The fraction 'rub' al-'ushr' means one quarter of one tenth, i.e., 2.5%. The proof is the hadith from Muslim: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awaq of silver' (an uqiya = 40 dirhams, so 5 uqiya = 200 dirhams) and similar hadith for gold. The author uses the term 'wajib' rather than 'fard', following al-Quduri, because some details of zakat (such as exact amounts) are based on ahad hadith. However, Sayyid Nukran and others argued that the measures of zakat are mutawatir (mass-transmitted) like the Qur'an and rak'at, so denying them would be disbelief. The passage emphasizes that zakat is only due on nisab; any amount below that, even a slight deficiency, has no zakat.

Key Terms
ربع العشر (rub' al-'ushr): One quarter of one tenth, i.e., 2.5%. The standard zakat rate for gold and silver.
نصاب (nisab): Minimum threshold for zakat: 200 dirhams of silver or 20 mithqals of gold.
وجوب (wujub): The legal obligation. Here used to describe zakat, with a debate whether it is fard or wajib.
أوقية (uqiya): A weight measure equal to 40 dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 5 dirhams (quarter of a tenth)
C) 2.5 dirhams (one-fortieth)
D) 1 dirham (one-two hundredth)

Key Takeaway
Zakat on gold and silver is obligatory at 2.5% of the nisab (200 dirhams silver or 20 mithqals gold), as established by hadith and agreed upon in the Hanafi school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Advancing Zakat Before Crop Growth
Intra-Hanafi dispute with causal analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad al-Shaybani's positions on early zakat payment and identify the key difference in their definition of the cause (sabab).

Core Idea
Early zakat payment is ikhtilaf: the cause is either potential or actual growth.

Can you pay zakat on your crops before they have even grown? This question reveals a subtle but consequential disagreement within the Hanafi school between two of its founding imams. In this lesson, we examine the reasoning of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether the cause (sabab) for zakat on land is established at the time of sowing or only when actual growth occurs. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens our ability to identify the role of ta'lil (causal reasoning) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Early payment of zakat on agricultural produce: Abu Yusuf permits it, Muhammad al-Shaybani forbids it.
Both are Hanafi imams; the dispute is intra-madhhab.
2
Compare definitions of the cause (sabab)
Abu Yusuf: cause is the land's potential for growth (al-ard al-namiya bi al-quwwa). Muhammad: cause is actual growth (bi haqiqat al-nama').
The definition of the 'illa drives the ruling.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
Both use qiyas: the 'illa is the land's productivity. Abu Yusuf: productivity is achieved after farming. Muhammad: productivity requires actual growth.
The difference is in the tahqiq al-manat (identification of the cause).
4
Apply the dispute to practice
If one pays early according to Abu Yusuf, the zakat is valid; according to Muhammad, it is invalid and must be repeated.
Practical consequence (thamarah) is whether the obligation is discharged.
5
Note the commentator's position
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq says the best is not to advance payment due to ikhtilaf, but he has not seen an explicit transmission.
This suggests caution is preferred, though not absolutely binding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوزه أبو يوسف لأن السبب الأرض النامية وبعد الزراعة صارت نامية، ورده محمد بأن السبب الأرض النامية بحقيقة النماء فيكون التعجيل قبلها واقعاً قبل السبب فلا يجوز . كذا في الولوالجية . ولا يخفى أن الأفضل لصاحب المال عدم التعجيل للاختلاف في التعجيل عند العلماء ولم أره منقولاً والله أعلم بالصواب وإليه المرجع والمآب .
And Abu Yusuf permitted it because the cause is the productive land, and after farming it became productive. Muhammad rejected (this) because the cause is the land productive in its true growth, so advancing (payment) before it occurs is before the cause, thus not permissible. As is in al-Walwaljiyyah. And it is not hidden that the best for the wealth owner is not to advance (payment) due to the difference of opinion among scholars regarding advancing (payment); and I have not seen it transmitted; and Allah knows best the truth, and to Him is the return and ultimate destination.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage records a notable intra-Hanafi disagreement concerning the permissibility of paying zakat on agricultural produce before the crop has actually grown, i.e., paying the zakat early at the time of sowing. Abu Yusuf allows it, reasoning that the cause of obligation is the land's potential for growth, and after farming, the land has become productive in fact. In contrast, Muhammad al-Shaybani disallows it, arguing that the cause is the land's actual growth (true growth), not mere potential; thus, paying zakat before the cause exists is like paying before the obligation has arisen, which is invalid. The commentator, after citing this dispute from al-Walwaljiyyah, notes that the preferable practice for a wealth owner is to avoid early payment because of the disagreement among scholars. However, he adds that he has not seen this transmitted (as a preferred view). The ruling influences practical fiqh: if one pays early, it may need to be repeated if it does not fulfill the obligation according to Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
تعجيل (ta'jil): Advancing the payment of zakat before the cause of obligation (e.g., growth of crops) materializes.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation, here the land's growth.
نماء (nama'): Growth or increase; the condition that makes the land productive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the cause is actual growth, and early payment occurs before the cause exists
C) Because the nisab has not been reached
D) Because Abu Yusuf disagreed

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of early zakat payment hinges on whether the cause (sabab) is defined as potential growth or actual growth, a legitimate point of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Zakat on Gold and Silver: Nisab, Rate, and Scope
Ruling with proof: nisab, rate, and extension to all forms.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the nisab and rate for zakat on gold and silver and explain why the ruling applies to bullion and jewelry, citing the relevant hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Zakat on gold and silver is wajib at 2.5% on any form — coins, bullion, or jewelry — once nisab is reached.

This lesson establishes the foundational zakat ruling for precious metals. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq sets the nisab and rate, and the commentator expands to clarify that all forms — coined, uncoined, and even jewelry — are subject to zakat. You will learn the textual proofs from the Sunnah that underpin this obligation and understand the Hanafi position that distinguishes between gold/silver and other valuables.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The matn begins by stating that zakat is obligatory on 200 silver dirhams and 20 gold dinars at a rate of 1/40 (2.5%). It then explicitly extends this to pure bullion (tibr), jewelry (hily), and utensils (aniya). Note that the ruling applies to all forms of gold and silver, whether shaped or unshaped.
2
Understand the nisab amounts
The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams (equivalent to 5 awaq, as per the hadith). For gold, it is 20 dinars (20 mithqals). The rate is fixed: 5 dirhams on 200, and half a mithqal on 20. The commentator clarifies the linguistic point that 'ushr' means tenth, and the required amount is a quarter of a tenth.
3
Analyse the proof for the nisab
The commentator cites the hadith from Muslim: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awaq of silver.' This explicitly sets the lower threshold. The nisab for gold is established by analogy and by specific hadiths from 'Ali and others. Recognise that the Hanafi school uses ahad hadiths (zanni al-thubut) for these quantities, which is why the obligation is classified as wajib, not fard.
The hadith is quoted in Arabic in the passage.
4
Examine the proof for jewelry
The commentator brings the hadith of 'A'ishah: when she wore fataqat (rings without gemstones), the Prophet asked if she paid their zakat. When she said no, he warned that they would be 'sufficient for you from the Fire' (i.e., punishment). This shows that jewelry of gold and silver is not exempt from zakat.
This proof directly addresses a common misconception that jewelry is exempt.
5
Note the limitation for other items
The passage ends by stating that for items other than gold and silver, zakat is only due if their value reaches the nisab in coined metal. This reinforces the principle that zakat on other trade goods is measured by the value in gold or silver.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Zakat is obligatory in two hundred dirhams and twenty dinars: a quarter of a tenth (2.5%), even if it is bullion, jewelry, or utensils. Then in every five according to its calculation. He said (obligatory in two hundred dirhams and twenty mithqals a quarter of a tenth) which is five dirhams in the two hundred and half a mithqal in the twenty. And 'ushr (tenth) with a dammah is one of the ten parts; rather a quarter of a tenth is obligatory due to the hadith of Muslim: 'There is no sadaqah on less than five awaq of silver' and the uqiyah is forty dirhams as al-Daraqutni narrated. And due to the hadith of 'Ali and others regarding gold. He said (even if it is bullion or jewelry) as a clarification that there is no difference between coined and uncoined, like the mahr shar'i. And the proof of the obligation of zakat on jewelry are hadiths in the Sunan, including his saying ﷺ to 'A'ishah when she adorned herself with fataqat: 'Do you pay their zakat?' She said: 'No.' He said: 'They are sufficient for you from the Fire.' Fataq is plural of fatkhah, which is a ring without a gemstone.

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the core ruling on zakat for gold and silver, with its proofs. The matn states that zakat is wajib on 200 dirhams or 20 dinars at the rate of 1/40 (2.5%), and that the ruling applies equally to bullion, jewelry, and utensils. The commentator clarifies that the word 'tibr' means raw gold or silver before being shaped, and 'hily' is women's jewelry. This ruling is based on established hadiths: the Prophet ﷺ fixed the nisab of silver at five awaq (200 dirhams) and analogously for gold at 20 mithqal. The hadith of 'A'ishah explicitly teaches that jewelry of gold and silver is subject to zakat, as the Prophet warned that if its zakat is not paid, it will be a source of punishment. The commentator also notes that for items other than gold and silver, zakat is only due if their value reaches the nisab in coined metal. This passage thus establishes both the textual basis and the scope of zakat on precious metals.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Gold or silver before being shaped into coins or ornamentation.
حلي (hily): Women's jewelry made of gold or silver.
نصاب (nisab): The minimum amount of wealth that triggers zakat obligation, here 200 dirhams (silver) or 20 dinars (gold).

Key Takeaway
Zakat on gold and silver is obligatory at 2.5% when one possesses the nisab (200 dirhams silver or 20 dinars gold), regardless of whether the metal is coined, bullion, or jewelry.

Zakat on Fractions Above Nisab: Every Fifth
Explains zakat calculation for fractional units above nisab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the zakat due on amounts exceeding the nisab for both silver and gold, applying the fractional khams unit.

Core Idea
Zakat is calculated proportionally: every additional 40 dirhams (or 4 dinars) incurs the same rate.

The nisab is the minimum threshold for zakat. But what happens when your wealth exceeds the nisab? This passage clarifies that zakat applies proportionally to every additional fractional unit—specifically, every 'khams' (fifth) of the nisab. For silver, that's every 40 dirhams; for gold, every 4 dinars. Understanding this ensures accurate zakat calculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nisab for silver and gold
Recall that the nisab for silver is 200 dirhams, for gold 20 dinars.
2
Define the khams unit
A khams is one-fifth of the nisab: 40 dirhams for silver, 4 dinars for gold.
The term 'khams' literally means 'fifth'.
3
Apply the zakat rate to each full khams
For each full 40 dirhams above nisab, pay 1 dirham (2.5% of 40). For each full 4 dinars above nisab, pay 2 qirats (1 qirat = 1/20 dinar, so 2 qirats = 0.1 dinar = 2.5% of 4 dinars).
This maintains the 2.5% rate proportionally.
4
Note the exemption for incomplete khams
If the excess is less than a full khams, no zakat is due on that fraction, even if the deficiency is slight.
This prevents fractional over-calculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ثم في كل خمس بحسابه) بضم الخاء المعجمة أحد الأجزاء الخمسة وهو أربعون من المائتين وأربعة مثاقيل من العشرين دينارا، فيجب في الأول درهم، وفي الثاني قيراطان . أفاد المصنف أنه لا شيء فيما نقص عن الخمس ولو كان نقصاناً يسيراً يدخل بين الوزنين.
His saying (Then in every five according to its calculation) with a dammah on the kha' one of the five parts, which is forty from the two hundred and four mithqals from the twenty dinars. So in the first (forty dirhams) one dirham is obligatory, and in the second (four dinars) two qirats. The author conveyed that there is nothing (due) on what is less than a fifth, even if the deficiency is slight, falling between the two weights.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This short passage explains the zakat due on fractions above the nisab. The term 'khams' (fifth) refers to one-fifth of the nisab: for silver, a fifth of 200 dirhams is 40 dirhams; for gold, a fifth of 20 dinars is 4 dinars. The commentator clarifies that for every additional 40 dirhams over the nisab, one dirham of zakat is due (i.e., the same rate of 2.5% applies proportionally). For gold, every additional 4 dinars requires two qirats (a qirat being 1/20 of a dinar). The note also states that amounts less than these fractions are exempt, even if the deficiency is very small. This ruling is based on the general principles of zakat calculation and ensures that the zakah is computed in a straightforward fractional manner according to the nisab units.

Key Terms
خمس (khams): Here, one-fifth of the nisab: 40 dirhams for silver, 4 dinars for gold.
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight for gold; 1 qirat = 1/20 of a dinar.
مثقال (mithqal): A unit of weight; here equivalent to a dinar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Zakat on savings above nisab is calculated by adding 1 dirham for every additional 40 dirhams (silver) or 2 qirats for every additional 4 dinars (gold), with incomplete fractions exempt.

Zakat on All Forms of Gold and Silver: Coins, Ingots, Jewelry
Ruling plus proof and intra-madhhab detail

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that zakat is wajib on all forms of gold and silver (coin, ingot, jewelry, vessels) and explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha, as well as identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the method of payment.

Core Idea
All gold and silver—coined, ingot, or jewelry—carry wajib zakat; the Prophet warned Aisha about her rings.

A common misconception is that jewelry for personal use is exempt from zakat. This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʼiq dispels that notion by citing the Prophet’s warning to Aisha and establishing that zakat is wajib on every form of gold and silver, regardless of shape or purpose. It also delves into a technical nuance: how to pay zakat on a silver vessel when the owner wishes to pay from its value rather than the item itself—a point of ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scope of Zakat on Gold/Silver
The passage explicitly states that zakat is wajib on gold and silver whether minted ( مصكوك ), in ingot form ( تبر ), or as jewelry ( حلي ). Note that this includes any object made of gold or silver, regardless of use: trade, spending, or adornment.
2
Define Key Terms: Tibr and Hiliy
Tibr is gold and silver before being forged. Hiliy is women's ornaments of gold/silver; it excludes gems/pearls. Compare with the definition in oaths (yamīn) where hiliy includes all ornaments.
3
Examine the Hadith Proof
The passage quotes the Prophet’s statement to Aisha about her rings ( فتخات : rings without stones). The question “Do you give their zakat?” followed by the warning “It is sufficient for you from the Fire” indicates obligation. Classify this hadith as ahad (zanni al-thubut) and note that the Hanafi school thus considers zakat wajib (not fard).
4
Analyze the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Payment Method
For a silver vessel over nisab, two views: Muhammad requires converting to gold when paying from value; Abu Hanifa allows paying silver from outside the vessel because weight is the standard. Both agree that paying gold from outside (not the vessel) is invalid because quality matters when exchanging different metals.
The muftā bihī is Abu Hanifa’s view: payment should be based on weight of the same metal, not conversion to gold.
5
Apply the Ruling to Modern Scenarios
Today, all gold and silver assets—jewelry, bars, coins, utensils—are subject to zakat as long as they reach nisāb and haul is complete. Exceptions: non-gold/silver items become zakatable only if their value reaches nisāb of coined metal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الزكاة باب زكاة المال مع لأنه وقع الشك في كمال النصاب فلا يحكم بكماله الشك . كذا في البدائع قوله (ولو تبرا أو حليا) بيان لعدم الفرق بين المصكوك وغيره كالمهر الشرعي. وفي غير الذهب والفضة لا تجب الزكاة ما لم تبلغ قيمته نصاباً مصكوكاً من أحدهما لأن لزومها مبني على المتقوم، والعرف أن تقوم بالمصكوك، وكذا نصاب السرقة احتيالاً للدك. قال في ضياء الحلوم: التبر الذهب والفضة قبل أن يصاغا ويعملا. وحُلي المرأة معروف وجمعه حلى وحلى بضم الحاء وكسرها قال تعالى من حليهم [الأعراف : ١٤٨] يقرأ بالواحد والجمع بضم الحاء وكسرها اهـ. والمراد بالحلي هنا ما تتحلى به المرأة من ذهب أو فضة، ولا يدخل الجوهر واللؤلؤ بخلافه في الإيمان فإنه ما تتحلى به المرأة مطلقاً فتحنث بلبس اللؤلؤ أو الجوهر في حلفها لا تتحلى ولو لم یکن مرصعاً على المفتى به . ودليل وجوب الزكاة في الحلي أحاديث في السنن منها قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لعائشة لما تزينت له بالفتحات أتؤدين زكاتهن؟ قالت: لا. قال: هو حسبك من النار. والفتخات جمع فتخة وهي الخاتم الذي لا فص له. وفي المعراج : وأما حكم الزكاة في الحلي والأواني يختلف بين أداء الزكاة من عينها وبين أدائها من قيمتها مثلاً. له إناء فضة وزنه مائتان وقيمته ثلثمائة فلو زكى من عينه زكى ربع عشره ولو أدى من قيمته، فعند محمد يعدل إلى خلاف جنسه وهو الذهب لأن الجودة معتبرة أما عند أبي حنيفة لو أدى خمسة من غير الإناء سقطت عنه الزكاة لأن الحكم مقصور على الوزن، فلو أدى من الذهب ما يبلغ قيمته قيمة خمسة دراهم من غير الإناء لم يجز في قولهم جميعاً لأن الجودة متقومة عند المقابلة بخلاف الجنس فإن أدى القيمة وقعت عن القدر المستحق. كذا في الإيضاح وفي البدائع : تجب الزكاة في الذهب والفضة مضروباً أو تبراً أو حلياً مصوغاً أو حلية سيف أو منطقة أو لجام أو سرج أو الكواكب في المصاحف، والأواني وغيرها إذا كانت تخلص عن الإذابة سواء كان يمسكها للتجارة أو للنفقة أو للتجمل أولم ينو شيئاً اهـ.
Book of Zakat, Chapter of Zakat on Wealth. Because doubt occurred in completion of nisab, so completion is not ruled due to doubt. Thus in Bada'i'. He said (or if ingot or jewelry) an explanation that there is no difference between coined and other like the legal dower. And in other than gold and silver, zakat is not obligatory unless their value reaches a nisab of coined metal of one of them, because its obligation is based on being valuable, and the custom is to value by coined metal. Likewise the nisab of theft as a trick for the coinage. He said in Diya' al-Hulom: Ingot is gold and silver before they are forged and worked. And women's jewelry is known, its plural is hula and hila, with damm of ha and kasr, Allah said: 'from their ornaments' read as singular and plural with damm of ha and kasr. And what is meant by jewelry here is what a woman adorns herself with of gold or silver, and it does not include gems and pearls unlike in oaths, for there it is what a woman adorns herself with absolutely, so she breaks her oath by wearing pearls or gems in her swearing that she will not adorn herself, even if not set, according to the relied-upon fatwa. And the evidence for obligation of zakat on jewelry is hadiths in the Sunan, including his saying, peace be upon him, to Aisha when she adorned herself with fatahkhat: 'Do you give their zakat?' She said: No. He said: 'It is sufficient for you from the Fire.' And fatahkhat is plural of fatkhah, which is a ring without a stone. And in al-Mi'raj: As for the ruling of zakat on jewelry and vessels, it differs between paying zakat from the same item and paying from its value. For example, he has a silver vessel weighing two hundred and value three hundred; if he gives zakat from the same item, he gives one quarter of a tenth; and if he gives from its value, then according to Muhammad he converts to a different kind, which is gold, because quality is considered. As for Abu Hanifa, if he gives five dirhams from other than the vessel, zakat is dropped from him because the ruling is limited to weight. If he gives from gold the value of five dirhams from other than the vessel, it is not valid according to all of them, because quality is valuable when counter exchanging unlike the same kind. If he gives the value, it falls on the amount due. Thus in al-Idah. And in al-Bada'i': Zakat is obligatory on gold and silver, whether minted or ingot or jewelry wrought or ornament of sword or belt or bridle or saddle or stars in mushafs, and vessels and others if they are free from melting, whether he holds them for trade or for spending or for adornment or he did not intend anything. End.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hadith. It begins by stating that zakat on gold and silver applies to all forms—coin (مصكوك), ingot (تبر), and jewelry (حلي)—with no difference. For non-gold/silver items, zakat is only due if their market value reaches the nisab of coined gold or silver, because value is determined by custom. The author defines تبر as gold and silver before being shaped, and حلي as women's ornaments of gold or silver, excluding pearls and gems; this differs from oaths where adornment includes all ornaments. The evidence for zakat on jewelry is the Prophet's (صلى الله عليه وسلم) question to Aisha about zakat on her ornaments, saying they would suffice as fuel for Hell if not paid. The passage then clarifies a sub-issue: for a silver vessel, if one pays zakat from the vessel itself, it is by weight; if paying value, Muhammad requires converting to gold, while Abu Hanifa allows paying silver from outside the vessel. The final quote from البدائع confirms zakat on all forms regardless of intention.

Key Terms
تبر (tibr): Gold and silver before being forged or worked into a form.
حلي (hiliy): What a woman adorns herself with of gold or silver, excluding other materials like gems.
فتخة (fatkhah): A ring without a stone (signet ring).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the hadith evidence for zakat on jewelry according to the Hanafi school?
A) The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) said: 'Gold and silver are subject to zakat'.
B) He asked Aisha about her rings and warned of Hellfire if zakat is not paid.
C) The Sahaba unanimously agreed that jewelry is zakatable.
D) There is no direct hadith; the ruling is based on qiyas.

Key Takeaway
Zakat on gold and silver is wajib in all forms—coined, ingot, jewelry, or vessel—based on the Prophet's warning to Aisha, and the method of payment relies on weight, not market value, per Abu Hanifa's view.

Zakat on Fractions: The Hanafi Dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat on fractional amounts above the nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on zakat on fractions, apply the proofs to a given scenario, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa exempts fractions below a full five-unit increment; the Sahibayn require zakat on every increase.

When calculating zakat on cash, the nisab thresholds are well-known: 200 dirhams or 20 dinars. But what about amounts in between – say, 205 dirhams? Is the additional 5 dirhams subject to zakat? This seemingly minor question sparked a significant intra-Hanafi disagreement, with far-reaching practical consequences. In this lesson, we examine the proofs and applications of this dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core point of disagreement
Determine whether zakat is due on amounts above the nisab that are less than a complete five-unit increment (e.g., 1–39 dirhams above 200, or 1–4 dinars above 20).
Abu Hanifa says no; the Sahibayn say yes.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Examine the hadiths 'Do not take from fractions anything' and 'No sadaqah on less than forty.' Understand how these texts support exemption.
The term 'quarters' in the text refers to fractional amounts.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Consider the hadith 'On what exceeds two hundred, according to its calculation.' Note how this implies proportional zakat on every dirham.
The Sahibayn interpret this as including fractions.
4
Resolve the dispute: tarjih and mufta bihi
Learn why the Hanafi school ultimately adopted Abu Hanifa's view, citing ease and the explicit hadith exempting fractions.
Later authorities like Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah side with Abu Hanifa.
5
Apply the dispute to concrete scenarios
Work through the examples given: 205 dirhams over two years, and destruction of 20 dirhams from 200. See how the difference plays out.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is shown clearly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حزم «ليس فميا دون الأربعين صدقة ولأن الحرج مدفوع، وفي إيجاب الكسور ذلك لتعذر الوقوف. وفي المعراج : معنى الحديث الأول لا تأخذ من الشيء الذي يكون المأخوذ منه كسوراً فسماه كسوراً باعتبار ما يجب فيه، وقيل من زائدة وفيه نوع تأمل .اهـ. ومما ينبني على هذا الخلاف لو كان له مائتان وخمسة دراهم مضى عليها عامان عنده عليه عشرة، وعندهما خمسة لأنه و- تب عليه في العام الأول خمسة وثمن فبقي السالم من الدين في العام He said (then in every five according to its calculation) with damm of the kha, one of the five parts, which is forty from two hundred and four mithqals from twenty dinars. So on the first, one dirham becomes obligatory, and on the second, two qirats. The author indicated that nothing is on what is less than five, so the exempt portion from silver after the nisab is nine, the one who rejects it becomes a disbeliever? So his speech, i.e. the intended, is carried on the amounts that exceed two hundred dirhams and similar increases on the nisabs, because that was not established by tawatur but only by ahad hadiths. He said: (he gave zakat of a quarter of a tenth) i.e. he gives five dirhams whose value is seven and a half - and that is the issue of the jug coming soon. He said: (he called them fractions in consideration of what is obligatory in them) so it is of the type of mentioning the state and intending the place, for wealth is the place of zakat, thus in al-Sa'diyya. He said: (and in it there is some reflection) perhaps its aspect is that the direct object would be the word 'fractions' and 'something' remains without much benefit; also one of the conditions of its increase is that its genitive be that every five according to its calculation and the standard is their weight in payment and obligation, and in dirhams weighing seven is thirty-three? So if he owns a nisab and seventy-nine dirhams, then six is due and the rest is exempt, and thus between five to five is exempt in gold, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: zakat is obligatory on what increases according to its calculation without exemption, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'And on what exceeds two hundred, according to its calculation.' And he has his statement in the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Do not take from fractions anything,' and his statement in the hadith of Amr ibn Hazm: 'There is no sadaqah on what is less than forty.' And because hardship is repelled, and imposing zakat on fractions has difficulty due to inability to ascertain. And in al-Mi'raj: The meaning of the first hadith is 'do not take from the thing which the taken thing from is fractions,' so he called them fractions in consideration of what is obligatory in them, and it is said that 'min' is extra, and in it there is some reflection. End. And from what is built on this dispute: if he has two hundred and five dirhams and two years pass, according to Abu Hanifa, ten is due, and according to them, five, because in the first year five and one-eighth became due, so the remainder free from debt in the second year is two hundred minus an eighth, so no zakat is due; and according to him (Abu Hanifa), there is no zakat on fractions, so the remainder is two hundred, so on it another five. A dirham in al-Mukhtar al-Qadir. And also built on the dispute is destruction after the year: if twenty of two hundred dirhams are destroyed, there remain four dirhams according to him, and according to them four and a half. Thus in al-Mi'raj. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit: One is not to add one increase to another to complete forty dirhams or four mithqals according to Abu Hanifa, because zakat is not obligatory on fractions according to him; according to them, they are added because zakat is obligatory on fractions.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding zakat on fractional amounts (كسور) above the nisab. The matn states that zakat is due on every five units (i.e., every 40 dirhams above 200, or every 5 dinars above 20). The commentator explains that according to Abu Hanifa, nothing is due on surplus that is less than a full five-unit increment; such amounts are exempt (عفو). This is based on the hadith 'Do not take from fractions anything' and 'No sadaqah on less than forty.' The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that zakat is due on every increase proportionally, citing the hadith 'On what exceeds two hundred, according to its calculation.' They consider hardship (حرج) as a reason for exemption, but Abu Hanifa emphasizes the difficulty of precise calculation for fractions. The passage then gives practical applications: for 205 dirhams over two years, Abu Hanifa's ruling leads to 10 dirhams zakat, while the Sahibayn's leads to 5; and for destruction of 20 dirhams from 200, the remaining amount determines the difference. The final note from al-Muhit clarifies that increments are not aggregated to form a full nisab increment under Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
كسور (kusur): Fractional amounts above the nisab that are less than a full five-unit increment (e.g., 1-39 dirhams above 200, or 1-4 dinars above 20).
عفو (afw): Exempt portion of wealth on which no zakat is due, specifically the surplus less than a full increment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the zakat due on 245 dirhams?
A) 6.125 dirhams
B) 5 dirhams
C) 6 dirhams
D) 7 dirhams

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that no zakat is due on fractional amounts less than a complete five-unit increment above the nisab.

Zakat on Silver Vessels: Weight, Value, or Benefit?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat payment method

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on zakat payment for silver vessels and apply the mufta bihi view (weight) to calculate zakat.

Core Idea
For zakat on silver vessels, Abu Hanifa holds weight is the standard; Muhammad considers benefit to poor; Zafar uses value.

When paying zakat on a silver vessel, should you give its weight in silver, its market value, or the option that most benefits the poor? The three major Hanafi imams differ, and their disagreement has practical consequences for every crafted item. In this lesson, we examine each view, the examples that illustrate them, and a nuanced calculation that arises from the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
First, locate the three distinct opinions: Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf (weight), Zafar (value), Muhammad (benefit of the poor). Understand the basis for each.
2
Analyze the examples of payment with good and bad dirhams
The text gives two scenarios: paying bad dirhams for a debt of good ones, and good dirhams for bad ones. Determine which scholars accept each case and why the dispute matters.
Focus on the logic: weight is objective, benefit is subjective, value is measurable.
3
Apply the positions to a silver jug
Using the jug weighing 200 dirhams valued at 300, compute zakat under each view: weight (5 dirhams), value (7.5 dirhams), benefit (the higher of the two).
The nugget 'anfa' li al-fuqara' is key for Muhammad's view.
4
Enter the complex calculation from al-Siraj
Examine the multi-year zakat problem for 1000 dirhams, noting the fraction disputes between Abu Hanifa and the two companions. Understand the correction of the fractional error.
This step builds arithmetic precision required for faraid and zakat.
5
Synthesize: which view is mufta bihi?
Conclude that the weight standard (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) is the relied-upon position in the school, as affirmed by al-Hidayah and later texts.
The tarjih authority is from the majority of Hanafi works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (والمعتبر وزنهما أداء ووجوبا أما الأول وهو اعتبار الوزن في الأداء فهو قول أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف. وقال زفر تعتبر القيمة. وقال محمد : يعتبر الأنفع للفقراء حتى لو أدى عن خمسة دراهم جياد خمسة زيوفاً قيمتها أربعة جياد جاز عند الإمامين خلافاً لمحمد وزفر، ولو أدى أربعة جيدة قيمتها خمسة ردية عن خمسة ردية لا يجوز إلا عند زفر ولو كان إبريق فضة وزنه مائتان وقيمته بصياغته ثلاثمائة إن أدى من العين يؤدي ربع عشره وهو خمسة قيمتها سبعة. كذا . نكرة عند الجمهور خلافاً للأخفش :قلت وثم وجه آخر وهو أن يكون من الكسور بياناً لقوله «شيئاً» ثم رأيته في الحواشي السعدية قوله : (ومما يبتني على هذا الخلاف الخ) ويبتنى عليه أيضاً ما ذكره في السراج : رجل له ألف درهم حال عليها ثلاثة أحوال، فعند أبي حنيفة يجب في الأولى خمسة وعشرون في الثانية أربعة وعشرون وفي الثالثة ثلاثة وعشرون، وعندهما للأولى خمسة وعشرون وللثانية أربعة وعشرون وثلاثة أثمان درهم لأن الكسر خمسة عشر وللثالثة ثلاثة وعشرون ونصف وربع وثمن درهم ا هـ. ونقله في النهر كذلك. قال بعض الفضلاء : قوله وثمن درهم صوابه وخمس ثمن درهم. ونقله بعضهم وارتضاه وبين وجهه . قلت : وليس كذلك بل صوابه وثمن ثمن «درهم» لأن الفارغ عن الدين في الحول الثالث تسعمائة وخمسون درهماً وخمسة أثمان درهم ففي تسعمائة وعشرين ثلاثة وعشرون درهماً وفي ثلاثين ثلاثة أرباع درهم، وفي خمسة أثمان درهم ثمن ثمن درهم كما لا يخفى على الحاسب قوله : (وذكر في المحيط ( خ ) ذكر بعض المحشين عن حاشية الزيلعي لمير غني أن ما نقله في البحر
He said (and the standard is their weight in payment and obligation). As for the first, which is considering weight in payment, it is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Zafar said: value is considered. And Muhammad said: what is most beneficial for the poor is considered, so that if he pays for five good dirhams five bad dirhams whose value is four good, it is valid according to the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) contrary to Muhammad and Zafar. And if he pays four good dirhams whose value is five bad for five bad, it is not valid except according to Zafar. And if there is a silver jug whose weight is two hundred and whose value with its craftsmanship is three hundred, if he pays from the same item, he pays a quarter of a tenth which is five whose value is seven. Thus. Nakira according the majority contrary to Akhfash. I said: and there is another aspect which is that the word 'from fractions' is an explanation of his word 'something'. Then I saw it in al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya. He said: (And from what is built on this dispute etc.) And built on it also what is mentioned in al-Siraj: A man has one thousand dirhams on which three years have passed. According to Abu Hanifa, in the first year twenty-five is due, in the second twenty-four, and in the third twenty-three. According to them (the two), for the first year twenty-five, for the second twenty-four and three-eighths of a dirham because the fraction is fifteen, and for the third twenty-three and a half and a quarter and an eighth of a dirham. End. And al-Nahr quoted it likewise. Some virtuous scholars said: his statement 'and an eighth of a dirham' is correct as 'and five-eighths of a dirham'. Some narrated it and approved it and explained its basis. I said: it is not so, but the correct is 'and an eighth of an eighth of a dirham' because the amount free from debt in the third year is nine hundred fifty dirhams and five-eighths of a dirham, so in nine hundred twenty, twenty-three dirhams, in thirty, three-quarters of a dirham, and in five-eighths of a dirham, an eighth of an eighth of a dirham, as is not hidden from the calculator. He said: (And it is mentioned in al-Muhit) - some commentators mentioned from the margin of al-Zayla'i for Mir Ghani that what was quoted in al-Bahr...
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage continues the dispute about zakat payment standards, specifically for silver vessels. The author explains that the standard for both obligation and payment is weight (وزن) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Zafar holds that value (قيمة) is considered, and Muhammad holds that the most beneficial for the poor (أنفع للفقراء) is considered. Examples illustrate: if one owes five good dirhams and pays five bad worth four good, it is valid according to the two imams but not according to Muhammad and Zafar; conversely, paying four good worth five bad for five bad is invalid except according to Zafar. The case of a silver jug (إبريق فضة) weighing 200 dirhams and valued at 300 dirhams is then given: if paying from the same item, zakat is 1/40 of the weight, i.e., 5 dirhams by weight (value 7 dirhams). The text then delves into a side discussion about the meaning of 'nakira' and its relevance, followed by a numerical application of the fraction dispute from al-Siraj involving 1000 dirhams over three years, showing the difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions. The final part corrects a calculation error regarding the third year, showing that the correct remainder is 950 5/8 dirhams, leading to zakat of 23 dirhams + 3/4 + 1/64 (i.e., 1/8 of 1/8) = 23.8125 dirhams.

Key Terms
إبريق (ibriq): A jug or vessel made of silver, used as an example for zakat on crafted items.
أنفع للفقراء (anfa' li al-fuqara'): The criterion for payment of zakat according to Imam Muhammad: the option that benefits the poor more, either by weight or value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By the market value of the vessel including craftsmanship.
B) By the weight of the silver content only.
C) By whichever amount is more beneficial to the poor.
D) No zakat is due on vessels unless they are for trade.

Key Takeaway
For zakat on gold and silver vessels, the Hanafi madhhab holds that the weight of the substance determines both the obligation and the payment amount, not the market value or craftsmanship.

Zakat on Fractional Surplus (Kusur): Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Explains the dispute on zakat for fractional surplus above nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on zakat on fractional surpluses (kusur) and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, including the proofs and practical consequences.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa exempts fractional surplus until a full 40 dirhams (or 5 dinars) is reached; the Sahibayn require proportional zakat on all excess.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: does zakat apply to small fractional amounts that exceed the nisab but are less than a full zakatable increment? While both sides agree on the nisab thresholds, they differ on how to treat the 'leftover' amounts. Understanding this difference is crucial for accurate zakat calculation in real-world scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi (Abu Hanifa) position
Abu Hanifa holds that fractions less than 40 dirhams (or 5 dinars) above the nisab are exempt (afw). Zakat is only due on each full 40 dirhams or 5 dinars increment.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that zakat is due on the entire excess proportionally, including fractions.
They base this on the general hadith about proportional calculation.
3
Analyse the proof of the Sahibayn
Their proof is the hadith: 'And for what exceeds two hundred, proportionally' (فبحسابه). They interpret this as requiring zakat on every part of the excess.
This is a general command that they apply to all amounts above nisab.
4
Analyse Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Do not take anything from the fractions' and the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm: 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty.' He also invokes the principle of repelling hardship (haraj) as calculating fractions is difficult.
The specific prohibition qualifies the general command.
5
Determine the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference affects the amount of zakat due. For example, on 205 dirhams: Abu Hanifa says 5 dirhams (since 200 gives 5, and 5 is exempt). The Sahibayn say 5 + 1/8 dirham (since 5/40 = 1/8). Also, combining two small surpluses: Abu Hanifa does not combine them to make 40; the Sahibayn do.
This has direct implications for zakat calculation in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإذا ملك نصاباً وتسعة وسبعين درهماً فعليه ستة والباقي عفو، وهكذا ما بين الخمس إلى الخمس عفو في الذهب وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يجب فيما زاد بحسابه من غير عفو لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام وفيما زاد على المائتين فبحسابه وله قوله عليه السلام في حديث معاذ لا تأخذ من الكسور شيئاً وقوله في حديث عمرو بن حزم «ليس فيما دون الأربعين صدقة» ولأن الحرج مدفوع، وفي إيجاب الكسور ذلك لتعذر الوقوف. وفي المعراج : معنى الحديث الأول لا تأخذ من الشيء الذي يكون المأخوذ منه كسوراً فسماه كسوراً باعتبار ما يجب فيه، وقيل من زائدة وفيه نوع تأمل .اهـ. ومما ينبني على هذا الخلاف لو كان له مائتان وخمسة دراهم مضى عليها عامان عنده عليه عشرة، وعندهما خمسة لأنه وجب عليه في العام الأول خمسة وثمن فبقي السالم من الدين في العام الثاني مائتان إلا ثمن فلا تجب فيه الزكاة وعنده لا زكاة في الكسور فيبقى السالم مائتين ففيها خمسة أخرى . درهم في المتح القدير. ويتبنى على الخلاف أيضاً الهلاك بعد الحول إن هلك عشرون من مائتي درهم بقي فيها أربعة دراهم عنده وعندهما أربعة ونصف كذا في المعراج. وذكر في المحيط : ولا يضم إحدى الزيادتين إلى الأخرى ليتم أربعين درهماً أو أربعة مثاقيل عند أبي حنيفة لأنه لا تجب الزكاة في الكسور عنده وعندهما يضم لأنها تجب في الكسور
If one possesses a nisab and seventy-nine dirhams, six are due and the rest is exempt. Similarly, between five and five (dinars) is exempt in gold. This is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: what exceeds is due proportionally without exemption, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'And for what exceeds two hundred, proportionally.' And he (peace be upon him) has his statement in the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Do not take anything from the fractions.' And his statement in the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm: 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty.' And because hardship is repelled, and in obligating fractions there is difficulty of ascertainment. In al-Mi'raj: The meaning of the first hadith is: do not take from a thing from which what is taken is fractions; so he called it fractions in consideration of what is due in it, and it was said 'min' is extra, and there is some contemplation. Ends. And from what is built on this difference: if one has two hundred and five dirhams and two years pass, according to (Abu Hanifa) ten is due on him, and according to them five, because five and one-eighth became due on him in the first year, so the remainder from the debt in the second year is two hundred minus one-eighth, so zakat is not due on it; and according to him (Abu Hanifa) there is no zakat on fractions, so the remainder is two hundred, in which there is another five dirhams. And built on the difference also: destruction after the year: if twenty are destroyed from two hundred dirhams, according to him four dirhams remain, and according to them four and a half. So in al-Mi'raj. And mentioned in al-Muhit: One of the two increases is not combined with the other to make forty dirhams or four mithqals according to Abu Hanifa, because zakat is not obligatory on fractions according to him; according to them they are combined because it is obligatory on fractions.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning zakat on fractional surpluses (kusur) beyond the nisab. The nisab for silver is 200 dirhams; for gold, 20 dinars. The rule: for every 40 dirhams above 200, one dirham is due; for every 5 dinars above 20, half a dinar. The question is whether zakat is due on fractions that are less than a full 40 or 5. Abu Hanifa holds that such fractions are exempt (afw), meaning no zakat is due on them until another 40 (or 5) is accumulated. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that zakat is due on the entire excess proportionally, including fractions. Their proof is the hadith 'and for what exceeds two hundred, proportionally' (meaning every 40 dirhams, one dirham), which they interpret generally. Abu Hanifa's proof includes the hadith of Mu'adh: 'Do not take anything from the fractions' and the hadith of 'Amr ibn Hazm: 'There is no sadaqah on less than forty.' He also argues hardship (haraj) is repelled, as exact calculation of fractions is difficult. The passage then provides consequences: two-year scenario and destruction of some dirhams after the year, showing how the difference plays out in practice. Finally, it mentions combining two surpluses: if one has two nisabs each with a small surplus, Abu Hanifa says the surpluses are not combined to make a full 40/5; Sahibayn say they are, since zakat is due on fractions. This is a key practical difference.

Key Terms
الكسور (al-kusur): Fractions or surplus amounts less than a full unit of zakatability (e.g., less than 40 dirhams or 5 dinars above the nisab).
العفو (al-afw): Exempt portion; surplus not subject to zakat until it reaches the next full threshold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person has 230 dirhams for one full year, how much zakat is due?
A) 5 dirhams (200 gives 5, remainder 30 exempt)
B) 5.75 dirhams (30/40 of a dirham added)
C) 6 dirhams (because 230/40 = 5.75, rounded up)
D) No zakat because the surplus is less than 40

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that fractional surplus (kusur) above nisab is exempt from zakat until it accumulates to a full 40 dirhams or 5 dinars.

Weight vs Value in Zakat Payment: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on payment standard with historical weight definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar on weight vs value in zakat payment and apply the mufta bihi ruling to given scenarios.

Core Idea
In zakat payment, weight is the standard, not value, according to the majority Hanafi view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a crucial intra-madhhab dispute: when paying zakat on silver or gold, do we consider the weight of the coins or their value? The answer affects how we pay with debased coins or crafted items. The passage also confirms that in obligation, weight is unanimously agreed upon, and provides the historical definition of the standard dirham.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that weight is the standard in payment. Muhammad considers what is most beneficial for the poor. Zufar considers value.
These are the three main views within the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the examples
Work through the three payment scenarios: paying debased coins for good ones, paying good coins for debased ones, and paying for a silver pitcher with value exceeding weight due to craftsmanship. Determine which position rules each scenario valid or invalid.
The examples clarify the practical consequences of each view.
3
Distinguish payment from obligation
In obligation (whether zakat is due), weight is unanimously agreed upon. If the weight of silver owned is below nisab (200 dirhams), no zakat even if value exceeds it.
This consensus simplifies the obligation rule.
4
Understand historical standardization
Learn how Umar standardized the dirham weight: ten dirhams weigh seven mithqals, each dirham is 14 qirats, each qirat is 5 barley grains.
This standard is used for zakat, theft nisab, mahr, and diyat.

And the standard is their weight in payment and obligation. As for the first, which is the consideration of weight in payment, it is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Zufar said: value is considered. Muhammad said: the most beneficial for the poor is considered; such that if he pays for five good dirhams, five debased dirhams whose value is four good ones, it is permissible according to the two imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad and Zufar. And if he pays four good dirhams whose value is five debased dirhams for five debased dirhams, it is not permissible except according to Zufar. And if there is a silver pitcher, weight two hundred, its value due to craftsmanship three hundred: if he pays from the same species, he pays one-tenth of its tenth, which is five, its value seven and a half; and if he pays five whose value is five, it is permissible according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). And Muhammad and Zufar said: it is not permissible unless he pays the surplus. So if he pays from a different species, value is considered by consensus. As for the second, which is the consideration of weight with respect to obligation, not number and value, it is agreed upon; such that if he has a silver pitcher of weight one hundred and fifty, and its value is two hundred, there is no zakat on it, and similarly gold. And in al-Bada'i: if silver is shared between two, then if the share of each reaches the amount of nisab, zakat is obligatory; otherwise not. And what is considered in partnership is what is considered in individual ownership. His saying: (And in dirhams, the weight is seven, meaning that ten of them weigh seven mithqals). And the mithqal, which is the dinar, is twenty qirats, and the dirham is fourteen qirats, and the qirat is five barley grains. That is, what is considered in dirhams etc. The origin of this is that dirhams were different in the time of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and in the time of Abu Bakr and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) in three categories: some were twenty qirats like the dinar, some were twelve qirats (three-fifths of a dinar), and some were ten qirats (half a dinar). The first had the weight of ten dinars, the second had the weight of six (i.e., each ten of them weighed six dinars), and the third had the weight of five (i.e., each ten of them weighed five dinars). Dispute arose among people regarding giving and receiving, so Umar took one dirham from each type and mixed them, making three equal dirhams, so each dirham came out as fourteen qirats. This practice has continued to this day in everything: in zakat, the nisab of theft, the dowry, and the estimation of blood money. And mentioned in al-Mughrib that this combination and striking was in the era of the Umayyads. And al-Marghinani mentioned that the dirham was like a stone (nawa) and became round in the time of Umar, and they wrote on it and on the dinar: 'There is no god but Allah, Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' and Nasir al-Dawla ibn Hamdan added. And in al-Ghaya: The dirham of Egypt is sixty-four grains, and it is larger than the zakat dirham, so the nisab from it is one hundred and eighty dirhams and two grains. And it was rebutted in Fath al-Qadir by saying there is doubt in it according to what they considered for the zakat dirham, because if he means by grain a barley grain, then the zakat dirham is seventy barley grains if ten weigh seven mithqals and the mithqal is one hundred barley grains, so it is then smaller, not larger. And if he means by grain two barley grains as its interpretation occurred in
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage discusses two main issues: (1) whether weight or value is the standard in zakat payment and obligation, and (2) the historical definition of the dirham weight. In payment, the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that weight is the standard: if one is obligated to pay five dirhams of zakat, he must give their weight in silver, not value. Zufar considers value, meaning he could give less weight if the coins are of higher value. Muhammad considers the most beneficial for the poor: if he pays with inferior coins, he must make up the value difference. The passage gives examples: paying five debased dirhams worth four good ones for five good dirhams—permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (since weight is equal), but not according to Muhammad and Zufar. Conversely, paying four good dirhams worth five debased ones—only Zufar permits. For a silver pitcher, if it weighs 200 dirhams but its value is 300 due to craftsmanship, one must pay 5 dirhams in weight (1/40 of 200), but its value is 7.5; if he pays 5 dirhams in weight (value 5), it is valid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. If he pays from a different metal, value is considered by consensus. In obligation, weight is agreed upon: if the silver in an object is less than the nisab in weight, no zakat, even if its value exceeds the nisab. Then the passage defines the standard dirham: ten dirhams weigh seven mithqals (dinars). The mithqal is 20 qirats, the dirham 14 qirats, and the qirat 5 barley grains. Historically, dirhams of different weights were used, so Umar standardized them by averaging three types, resulting in 14 qirats per dirham. This standard is used for zakat, theft nisab, mahr, and diyat. The passage concludes with a note on the Egyptian dirham being larger, and a critique from Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
المثقال (al-mithqal): Standard gold coin (dinar) weighing 20 qirats (about 4.25 grams). Used as reference for dirham weight.
القيراط (al-qirat): Unit of weight, equal to 5 barley grains (sha'irat). Used to define mithqal and dirham.
الزيوف (al-zyuf): Debased or counterfeit coins; inferior dirhams with less silver content.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Yes, because value exceeds nisab
B) No, because weight is below nisab (200 dirhams)
C) Yes, because craftsmanship value counts
D) No, because it is not pure silver

Key Takeaway
In zakat payment, the mufta bihi is to rely on weight as the standard, following Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, while in obligation, weight is unanimously agreed upon.

Paying Zakat with Goods of Different Value: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on zakat valuation and weight-based obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on paying zakat with goods of lower value and identify the operative position.

Core Idea
When paying from a different genus, value is binding; for same genus, weight governs obligation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a nuanced dispute among Hanafi imams about zakat payment when the goods given are of different value than what is owed. It also clarifies that weight, not count or market value, is the measure for nisab on silver and gold. We will examine both positions and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of dispute
The text considers a case: a person pays zakat by giving five items whose total value is five (equal to what is owed). The dispute centers on whether this is permissible if the items themselves are of a different type or lower weight.
Scenario: paying in kind with value equal but not the exact property.
2
State the two positions
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (indahuma) hold it is permissible. Muhammad al-Shaybani and Zufar require the deficiency to be paid if the goods are of lower value; they only allow payment of exact value without shortfall.
Opposing views within the same madhhab.
3
Analyze the consensus on value for different genus
When paying from a different genus (e.g., silver instead of gold), the text states that value is considered by consensus (ijma). This consensus supports the permissive view in the dispute, as value is the criterion for payment across genera.
Ijma strengthens Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's position.
4
Derive the rule for obligation based on weight
For silver and gold, the obligation of zakat depends on weight, not count or market value. Example: a silver pitcher weighing 150 dirhams (below nisab) incurs no zakat even if its market value is 200 dirhams.
Weight is the measure for nisab, not value.
5
Apply the rule to joint ownership
In joint ownership, each partner's share must independently reach the nisab by weight for zakat to be obligatory. The same rule applies as for individual ownership.
Partnership does not aggregate shares.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونصف، وإن أدى خمسة قيمتها خمسة جاز عندهما. وقال محمد وزفر : لا يجوز إلا أن يؤدي الفضل فلو أدى من خلاف جنسه تعتبر القيمة بالإجماع وأما الثاني وهو اعتبار الوزن في حق الوجوب دون العدد والقيمة فمجمع عليه حتى لو كان له إبريق فضة وزنها مائة وخمسون وقيمتها مائتان فلا زكاة فيها وكذا الذهب وفي البدائع ولو كانت الفضة مشتركة بين اثنين، فإن كان يبلغ نصيب كل واحد مقدار النصاب تجب الزكاة وإلا فلا، ويعتبر في حال الشركة ما يعتبر في حال الانفراد.
And half, and if he pays five whose value is five, it is permissible according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Muhammad and Zufar said: it is not permissible unless he pays the extra. If he pays from a different genre, value is considered by consensus. As for the second [point], which is the consideration of weight regarding obligation, not count or value, it is agreed upon. So if he has a silver pitcher weighing one hundred fifty and worth two hundred, there is no zakat on it, and similarly for gold. In al-Bada'i: if silver is jointly owned by two, then if each one's share reaches the nisab, zakat is obligatory; otherwise not. And what is considered in the case of partnership is what is considered in the case of individual ownership.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the payment of zakat when the goods paid are of different value than what is owed. The matn states a ruling: if one pays five items worth five, it is valid according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. However, Muhammad and Zufar disagree, requiring that the deficiency be made up. The text clarifies that when paying from a different genus (jins), value is considered by consensus. It then moves to a settled rule: for obligation of zakat on silver and gold, weight is considered, not count or value. Thus, a silver pitcher weighing 150 dirhams (below nisab) has no zakat even if its market value is 200 dirhams. Finally, it addresses joint ownership: each partner's share must individually reach the nisab for zakat to be obligatory, applying the same rule as for individual ownership.

Key Terms
عندهما (indahuma): Refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two major disciples of Abu Hanifa.
محمد وزفر (Muhammad wa Zufar): Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam Zufar, both Hanafi scholars.
الوزن (al-wazn): Weight, the basis for determining nisab for silver and gold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For zakat on silver and gold, weight is the sole measure of nisab, and when paying from a different genus, value is the standard.

Standard Dirham Weight for Zakat Nisab
Historical and fiqhi determination of the standard dirham weight for nisab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the standard weight of the legal dirham (14 qirats), explain its basis in the practice of Caliph Umar, and apply the rule for adding increments when calculating nisab for silver.

Core Idea
The legal dirham weighs 14 qirats; nisab for silver is 200 such dirhams, as determined by Umar's consensus.

Zakat on silver requires knowledge of the dirham's weight. This lesson traces the origin of the legal standard to Caliph Umar's amalgamation of three coin types, producing a uniform dirham of 14 qirats. It also addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when one owns two separate nisabs with small surpluses, how those surpluses affect zakat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its proof
The passage establishes that the legal dirham weighs 14 qirats (each qirat = 5 barley grains). The proof is Caliph Umar's practical consensus: he blended three coin types to create equal dirhams, and the practice continued.
This is a dalil naqli (transmitted evidence) based on ijma (consensus).
2
Trace the historical development
The text recounts that before Umar, dirham weights varied (20, 12, 10 qirats). Umar standardized by melting and mixing, producing 14-qirat dirhams. This standard applies to zakat, theft nisab, mahr, and blood money.
The discussion of later Egyptian dirhams shows that regional variations existed.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on increments
If someone has two separate nisabs (e.g., 200 dirhams each) and each has a surplus (ziyadah), do the surpluses combine to form a new nisab? Abu Hanifa says yes if the combined surplus reaches 40 dirhams (since zakat is not owed on fractions); Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no, zakat is due on fractions proportionally.
The text notes that the author inclines to Abu Hanifa's view, but later practice favors the Sahibayn.
4
Apply the standard to modern calculations
Knowing that the legal dirham is 14 qirats = 70 barley grains, and 10 dirhams = 7 mithqals (one mithqal = 100 barley grains), the nisab of silver is 200 × 70 barley grains. Convert to grams using the weight of one barley grain.
This step is practical for determining contemporary nisab values.

قوله (وفي الدراهم وزن سبعة وهو أن تكون العشرة منها وزن سبعة مثاقيل) والمثقال وهو الدينار عشرون قيراطاً والدرهم أربعة عشر قيراطاً والقيراط خمس شعيرات أي المعتبر في الدراهم إلى آخره والأصل فيه أن الدراهم كانت مختلفة في زمن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وفي زمن أبي بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما على ثلاث مراتب : فبعضها كان عشرين قيراطاً مثل الدينار، وبعضها كان اثني عشر قيراطاً ثلاثة أخماس الدينار وبعضها عشرة قراريط نصف الدينار. فالأول وزن عشرة من الدنانير والثاني وزن ستة أي كل عشرة منه وزن ستة من الدنانير، والثالث وزن خمسة أي كل عشرة منه وزن خمسة من الدنانير فوقع التنازع بين الناس في الإيفاء والاستيفاء فأخذ عمر من كل نوع درهماً فخلطه فجعله ثلاثة دراهم متساويه، فخرج كل درهم أربعة عشر قيراطاً فبقي العمل عليه إلى يومنا هذا في كل شيء في الزكاة ونصاب السرقة والمهر وتقدير الديات. وذكر في المغرب أن هذا الجمع والضرب كان في عهد بني أمية. وذكر المرغيناني أن الدرهم كان شبيه النواة وصار مدوراً على عهد عمر فكتبوا عليه وعلى الدينار «لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله وزاد ناصر الدولة ابن حمدان ». وفي الغاية : إن درهم مصر أربعة وستون حبة وهو أكبر من درهم الزكاة فالنصاب منه مائة وثمانون درهماً وحبتان. وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأن فيه نظراً على ما اعتبروه في درهم الزكاة لأنه إن أراد بالحبة الشعيرة فدرهم الزكاة سبعون شعيرة إذا كان العشرة وزن سبعة مثاقيل والمثقال مائة شعيرة فهو إذن أصغر لا أكبر، وإن أراد بالحبة أنه شعيرتان كما وقع تفسيرها في والنهر عن المحيط غلط في النقل وأن المذكور في غاية السروجي عن المحيط أنه تضم إحدى الزيادتين إلى الأخرى عنده ولا تضم عند عكس ما نقله هنا من ذكر الخلاف ا هـ. . أقول : وقد راجعت المحيط فرأيته كما نقله السروجي ووجهه ظاهر لأنه إذا كانت الزكاة واجبة في الكسور عندهما لم يظهر فائدة للضم تأمل . ثم رأيت في البدائع مثل ما نقلناه عن المحيط ونصه : فإن كان على كل من النصابين زيادة فعند أبي يوسف ومحمد لا يجب ضم إحدى الزيادتين إلى الأخرى لأنهما يوجبان الزكاة في الكسور بحسبها، وأما عند أبي حنيفة ينظر إن بلغت منهما أربعة مثاقيل وأربعين درهماً فكذلك، وإن كانت أقل من أربعة مثاقيل وأقل من أربعين درهماً يجب ضم إحدى الزيادتين إلى الأخرى ليتم أربعة مثاقيل وأربعين درهماً لأن الزكاة لا تجب عنده في الكسور ا هـ . قوله : (وذكره في فتح القدير الخ) ظاهر كلام المؤلف الميل إليه، وفي السراج إلا أن الأول وهو أربعة عشر قيراطاً عليه الجم الغفير والجمهور الكثير وإطباق كتب المتقدمين والمتأخرين .
His statement: (And regarding dirhams, the weight is seven, meaning that ten of them weigh seven mithqals). The mithqal, which is the dinar, is twenty qirats, and the dirham is fourteen qirats, and the qirat is five barley grains. That is the standard for dirhams etc. The origin of this is that dirhams varied in the time of the Prophet ﷺ and in the time of Abu Bakr and Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, in three categories: some were twenty qirats like the dinar, some were twelve qirats (three-fifths of a dinar), and some were ten qirats (half a dinar). The first weighed ten dinars, the second weighed six dinars per ten, and the third weighed five dinars per ten. People disputed over payment and receipt, so Umar took one dirham from each type, mixed them, and made them into three equal dirhams, so each came out as fourteen qirats. This practice has continued to this day in everything: zakat, nisab of theft, dowry, and assessment of blood money. Al-Mughrib mentions that this melting and striking occurred during the Umayyad period. Al-Marghinani mentioned that the dirham was like a date pit and became round in Umar's time, and they inscribed on them and on the dinar: 'La ilaha illa Allah Muhammad Rasul Allah' and Naser al-Dawla ibn Hamdan added something. In al-Ghayah: The Egyptian dirham is sixty-four grains and is larger than the zakat dirham, so its nisab is one hundred eighty dirhams and two grains. Fath al-Qadeer criticizes this, saying it is questionable given what they consider for the zakat dirham: if he means barley grains, then the zakat dirham is seventy grains (since ten weigh seven mithqals and a mithqal is one hundred grains), so it is smaller, not larger. If he means two barley grains (as interpreted elsewhere), then... (the text becomes unclear). The author notes a mistake in al-Muhit regarding the transfer, and that what is mentioned in Ghayat al-Saruji from al-Muhit is that one of the increments is added to the other according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad – the opposite of what is reported here. The author says: I checked al-Muhit and found it as al-Saruji stated; the rationale is clear since if zakat is obligatory on fractions according to them, there is no benefit in adding. Then he saw in al-Bada'i similar to what we quoted from al-Muhit: If each of the two nisabs has an increment, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, one increment is not added to the other because they obligate zakat on fractions proportionally. According to Abu Hanifa, if the increments together reach four mithqals and forty dirhams, similarly no addition; if less than that, the increments must be added to complete four mithqals and forty dirhams, because zakat is not obligated on fractions in his view. The author's statement (and he mentioned it in Fath al-Qadeer etc.) shows his inclination towards the first view. In al-Siraj, the first view (fourteen qirats) is adopted by the great multitude and majority of early and later texts.
Source pages p. 396

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe into the standard weight of dirhams for zakat and related rulings. It begins by defining the legal dirham: ten dirhams weigh seven mithqals (dinars), each dirham is 14 qirats, each qirat is five barley grains. The historical origin: dirhams varied in the Prophet's time; Umar standardized them by mixing three types to produce a uniform dirham of 14 qirats. This standard applies to zakat nisab, theft nisab, mahr, and diyah. The text then discusses later variations: Egyptian dirhams being larger, and a critique from Fath al-Qadeer. It also includes an intra-Hanafi dispute on increments (ziyadat): if one has two types of wealth each reaching nisab with an increment, Abu Hanifa requires adding increments to complete the nisab if they fall short of 4 mithqals and 40 dirhams; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not add, as they obligate zakat on fractions. The author inclines to the view of Abu Hanifa. Finally, it concludes that the 14-qirat standard is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
قيراط (qirat): A unit of weight; 1 qirat = 5 barley grains; 1 dirham = 14 qirats; 1 dinar = 20 qirats.
مثقال (mithqal): The weight of one dinar; equal to 20 qirats or 100 barley grains.
الزيادة (al-ziyadah): An increment above the nisab that does not by itself constitute a new nisab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 20 qirats; based on the weight of the dinar.
D) 10 qirats; based on the lightest coin in circulation.

Key Takeaway
The legal dirham is fixed at 14 qirats by the consensus of the Companions, and this weight is the basis for the nisab of silver and other Shar'i measurements.
